0 Executive Summary

0.1 Project Information
     The project integrates the twin concepts of low-carbon and nature-positive urban
development to enhance urban livability and mitigate climate change, with a focus on
biodiversity enhancement in the project areas while reducing carbon emissions from the
transportation and wastewater sectors and enhancing the carbon sequestration capacity of local
ecosystems. Climate adaptation and resilience will be enhanced by improving ecosystems and
implementing nature-based solutions. The project will also improve the accessibility and
ecotourism development of Aha National Wetland Park and provide opportunities for
sustainable economic development in the project areas. At the same time, the project will
support studies on low-carbon and biodiversity-related policies, spatial planning and capacity
building, including the establishment and improvement of carbon emissions monitoring and
accounting system that promotes the achievement of carbon emission reduction targets as well
as the eventual realization of carbon peaking and carbon neutrality goals, and explore the
innovative model for green and low-carbon development in the city of Guiyang.

     This report is based on the Environmental Impact Assessment (Draft) prepared in March
2025, in conjunction with the contents and conclusions in the Domestic Environmental Impact
Assessment (DEIA) prepared in 2025, so as to form the final version of the EIA (including the
Environmental Management Plan (EMP)).

0.2 Description of Project Activities
     The project consists of three components, respectively focusing on low-carbon urban
mobility, nature-positive urban solutions and city-wide institutional strengthening, as listed
below:

     Component 1: Low-carbon urban mobility for enhanced livability. This component
will finance improvements and constructions around the Aha Lake, on: (i) Non-Motorized
Transport (NMT) network and connections to city-wide green network; (ii) public transit
connections (roads upgrade for last mile bus connections to metro stations), facilities (such as
bus interchange, and integrated visitor and transit facilities) and services (intelligent transport
systems, and improving bus coverage, frequency and service); (iii) road connections to and
between key city thoroughfares; (iv) integrated visitor/parking facilities and amenities
including EV charging stations and bicycle stands; and (v) traffic and transport management.
The total GHG emissions reduction/avoidance amount is estimated at 14,390 tCO2e/year.

                                                 I
     Component 2: Nature-Positive Urban Solutions for Climate Mitigation, Adaptation,
and Biodiversity. This component will finance interventions to improve water quality, enhance
flood control, and conserve urban ecosystems and biodiversity. Activities include: (i)
improvements of wastewater and drainage works (e.g., sewers, stormwater open channels,
wastewater pump stations, small-scale wastewater treatment stations, installation of associated
monitoring system); (ii) improvement of supporting infrastructure and public facilities for Aha
National Wetland Park (e.g., water supply pipelines and pumping station, outdoor signposts);
(iii) restoration of selected terrestrial habitats (e.g., woodland in the existing ecological buffer
zones along the riverbank and around the lake) through structural and Nature-based Solution
(NbS) measures, such as erosion control, habitat bridges, culverts, afforestation and vegetation
restoration with native species; (iv) restoration of selected aquatic ecosystems in Aha Lake and
its tributaries by reintroducing endemic fish, benthic animals, and aquatic plant species,
introducing porous microhabitat mounds and modifying nearshore slope; (v) enhanced
biodiversity monitoring for the 100 km2 Aha Lake area on plants, birds, mammals, amphibians,
reptiles, etc. by using traditional visual survey methods (such as using cameras) as well as
environmental DNA (eDNA) approaches; and (vi) environmental management such as
awareness raising and sanitation measures. In the long term, this component will improve
resilience and livability of the project areas through better flood management and cooling
effects, job creation and innovative environmental and biodiversity conservation,
water/wastewater management, and eco-tourism development. The total GHG emissions
reduction amount is estimated at 78,410 tCO2e/year.

     Component 3: City wide institutional strengthening for low carbon and nature
positive urban development. This component will finance city-wide initiatives to support the
project's sustainability, including: (i) green account and prototype development, involving
software design, development, and testing of a mobile application, along with necessary
hardware; (ii) awareness-raising, capacity building, promotional, and citizen engagement
activities; (iii) technical analysis and development of urban spatial plans; (iv) research and
technical assistance for policies, regulations, and plans on carbon sequestration, carbon market
mechanisms, and low-carbon transport for vulnerable groups; and (v) project management,
capacity building, and coordination activities. This component aims to position Guiyang as a
front-runner in integrating low-carbon and nature-positive thinking into urban systems, policies
and communities.




                                                 II
0.3 Environmental Risk Rating
     The environmental risk level of the project is rated following the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework policy, considering the nature, type and scale of
proposed project activities, significance and sensitivity of anticipated impacts, and E&S
capacity of the implementation agency.

     According to the results of environmental and social risk screening, the proposed project
activities are largely small-scaled and scattered in and around Lake Aha (100km2), and the
construction activities under the project include the restoration of ecological buffer zones in the
Lake Aha Basin and the prevention and control of rural water pollution which are in small scale
and scattered, and the implementation of the project will benefit the environmental
improvements and biodiversity enhancement in the lake basin. However, some of the project
activities for NMT paths and habitat rehabilitation (occupying 446.90mu of the ecological red
line, including 300.58mu (0.20km2) located within the scope of Lake Aha National Wetland
Park) require construction within the ecological red line of key wetland. Though the project
will be in alignment with the Master Plan of Lake Aha National Wetland Park and its operation
phase will bring ecological benefits, construction activities are expected to cause short-term
negative environmental impacts, including the generation of dust, noise, wastewater and solid
waste, increase of soil erosion around the lake and along the targeted tributaries, ecological
impacts on local plants, wildlife and their habitats, risk of pests and diseases management and
invasion of foreign species during the implementation of greening works and ecological
restoration, Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) risks for construction workers, and traffic
disturbance and health risks for nearby communities. Since the project activities are largely
small-scaled and scattered in the 100km2 lake basin, the above negative environmental impacts
are generally temporary and site-specific, which can be mitigated to an acceptable level by
adopting specific mitigation measures during project construction and operation.

     Considering the above factors, the environmental risk level of this project is considered
"Substantial", and the negative environmental impacts generated by the project are easy to
predict and can be effectively avoided or controlled by adopting conventional mitigation
measures.




                                                III
0.4 Environmental Benefits of the Project
     The project addresses interconnected development issues by adopting a dual low-carbon
and nature-positive strategy and is anticipated to deliver the following environmental benefits
in the Aha Lake area and Guiyang Municipality.

0.4.1 To improve local environmental quality
     The project will support the construction of sewers, sewage pumping stations, and small
rural wastewater treatment facilities serving the lake basin, which is expected to reduce
pollutant discharge into the lake basin. With the project completion, the wastewater collection
rate of Aha Lake Basin can be increased from the current 50% to 100%, and the wastewater
treatment rate can be increased from the current 30% to 70%. In the short term, the
project-supported wastewater management activities will reduce the discharge of BOD by
1,873t/year, COD by 2,535 t/year, SS by 2,535 t/year, TN by 496 t/year, and TP by 49.6 t/year.
In the long term, the annual reduction of BOD is 3,461 tons, COD is 4,683 tons, SS is 3,868
tons, TN is 916 tons, and TP is 91.62 tons.

0.4.2 To enhance local biodiversity.
     The improvements of wastewater collection and treatment, restoration of selected
landscape/habitat, clearing and control of invasive species will help to improve the lake water
quality as well as aquatic and terrestrial ecosystems of the lake basin. The biodiversity
monitoring as part of the project will cover plants, birds, animals, amphibians, reptiles, etc.
With the revegetation of selected landscapes and improvements of forest quality around the
lake, the project is expected to strengthen the soil erosion control and improve the regional soil
structure, which will consequently facilitate the nutrient cycling in the soil, improve the
primary productivity of local ecosystems and contribute to the enhancement of local
biodiversity.

0.4.3 To increase climate mitigation and adaptation capacity of Guiyang City.
     Under the project, Component 2 is to provide nature-positive urban solutions for climate
mitigation, adaptation and biodiversity, while the design of Component 1 on low-carbon urban
mobility will be informed by ecosystem conservation and ensuring infrastructure is
nature-positive, complementing activities under Component 2. Climate mitigation risks from
the construction of two connection roads between major highways around Lake Aha are
reduced to low as in overall consideration with other project activities, there are no other
feasible lower carbon alternatives to create shorter and more efficient travel paths between


                                               IV
existing highways, while reducing congestion, improving traffic flow, and enabling more
efficient bus routing and transit times. According to the quantitative forecast, 15-20 percent of
private vehicle trips will be reduced through enhanced NMT and public transit access, and
30-35 percent of idle time will be decreased through improved traffic flow on upgraded
corridors, translating to a 20-25 percent reduction in direct fuel consumption. On climate
adaptation, Lake Aha and its tributaries aid flood risk management through increased water
retention (flood risks are higher in the built-up southern areas and central Guiyang). To
mitigate these risks, the design standards against 1 in 100 years floods will be adopted for all
project-supported infrastructure investments and facilities. The project will also adhere to
China Flood Control Standards, the Code for Design of Urban Flood Control Engineering,
technical specifications for permeable pavements, and the Code for Design of Stormwater
Control. Slope protection through planting endemic species will enhance stability and
anti-erosion capabilities. Subcomponent 3.2 will promote climate-informed land use planning,
preventing new residents or infrastructure in highly exposed areas. The project includes
investment in NBS for flood risk mitigation and is designed to enhance Guiyang's overall
resilience to climate change impacts, maintaining climate hazard risks at an acceptable level.

0.4.4 To enhance the livability of the project areas
     With the implementation of project-supported physical investments and research on
low-carbon and green development, the city’s livability will be enhanced. Meanwhile, the
project will also support activities for enhancing the public awareness and engagement on
biodiversity conservation, thus leading to the behavior changes of local communities.

0.4.5 To contribute to GHG emission reduction
     According to the FSR, with the implementation of proposed transport, water and
environment interventions to improve travel and energy efficiency, the total GHG emission
reduction of the project is estimated to reach approximately 92,800 tCO2e by project
completion and 2,784,000 tCO2e for a 30-year operation period of the infrastructure.

0.4.6 To showcase the care to female and ethnic minority groups by promoting carbon
peaking and carbon neutrality
     The Green and Low Carbon Smart Platform of Guiyang City and other activities under the
project will incorporate gender equality in the mainstream practice of carbon peaking and
carbon neutrality, actively conduct statistics and study on gender in terms of green travel and
green life, and discover the performance of female population in carbon emission reduction
through the perspective of cross-over analysis, in order to not only showcase the government’s
                                               V
care towards women, but also encourage them to participate in the cause of “carbon peaking
and carbon neutrality”. In the meantime, the propaganda will be strengthened by popularizing
the knowledge and relevant policies of “carbon peaking and carbon neutrality” to the ethnic
minority groups, the green and low carbon renovation of old urban areas will be accelerated to
improve the sense of fulfillment and happiness for the ethnic minority groups, so as to
showcase the government’s care towards the ethnic minority groups, and encourage them to
support the cause and development of “carbon peaking and carbon neutrality”.

0.5 Environmental Impact Analysis and Mitigation Measures
     At this stage, the Domestic Environmental Impact Assessment (DEIA) for the project has
been approved by Guiyang Municipal Ecology and Environment Bureau (including special
ecological assessment and special acoustic environmental assessment) in May 2025, based on
which it is concluded that the project activities are designed for environmental benefits and not
expected to cause significant impacts on the environment and local communities, and the
construction of the project is feasible from the perspective of environmental protection.

0.5.1 Environmental considerations in Project Design
     Though the project design work has no direct impact on the ecological environment,
during the FSR preparation, environmental considerations have been integrated to avoid,
minimize and mitigate the potential environmental impacts associated with project
implementation. This includes optimizing site selection and specific construction plans, as well
as choosing operation modes that reduce risks or negative effects on the environment. For
instance, optimized siting and routing reduce forest land occupation, and some sections of the
greenway use trestles or natural pavement to limit wildlife disruption. The project prioritizes
native topsoil and species to prevent invasive species, creating a plant community harmonious
with the Lake Aha Wetland environment. Additionally, it optimizes construction design to
reduce temporary works, implements soil and water conservation measures, and designs
pollution prevention and control for exhaust gas, wastewater, noise, and solid waste.

0.5.2 Environmental impacts and mitigation measures during the construction period
     Based on the findings of current FSR and special ecological assessment report, the
project's greenway, cycling station, Line C416 and sewage network around the lake are
partially located within the delineated ecological redline. Construction activities could pose
risks to wildlife, with the risks to introduce pests, diseases or foreign species, increase soil
erosion, and lead to the destruction of local vegetation and the disturbance of local habitats.
The project will permanently occupy 879.7mu of forestland but will not involve the core

                                               VI
protected area of the wetland park, and the activities within the eco-redline are all designed for
ecological restoration, ecotourism development and public education, not compromising the
functions of local ecosystems and in full compliance with the national ecological protection
redline regulations, other regulatory requirements and relevant governmental plans, plus the
project has gained the Letter of Review Opinions on the Limited Human Activities within the
Ecological Protection Red Line Involved under Guiyang Green Urban Development Project
issued by Guiyang City People’s Government, where the project proposal is approved. Except
for the permanent land occupation, all other negative ecological impacts of the project will be
temporary and site-specific. As mentioned above, the mitigation measures have been integrated
into the project design during preparation: (1) optimize the construction layout and reduce the
temporary land use; (2) optimize the construction plan, adopt green construction technology,
enhance the design of supports for high and steep slopes, reduce the surface excavation,
minimize vegetation destruction and disturbance to the sensitive ecosystems as far as possible;
(3) strengthen the training and management of construction workers, reasonably schedule the
construction and transportation activities, restrict the construction area and roads, implement
integrated pest management and alien species control measures, implement soil and water
conservation, timely restore local vegetation and habitats after temporary land use. After taking
these measures, the overall impacts on the environment during the construction period will not
be significant.

     In addition to the ecological impacts, the construction of transport network around Lake
Aha and wastewater network on the northeast side, will generate construction nuisance, with
the generation of dust, noise and increased traffic, and thus pose health and safety risks on
nearby communities, such as Zhulin Village and Jinshan Village. However, these impacts
during the construction period are temporary and site-specific. By implementing environmental
mitigation measures and maintaining effective communication with nearby residents, these
effects can be managed to an acceptable level.

0.5.3 Environmental impacts and mitigation measures during the operational period
     The environmental impact during the operation period includes risks from increased
tourists and potential disturbance to local habitats and wildlife, as well as increased noise,
exhaust, and traffic safety issues with the increase of traffic volume. However, since the project
activities are scattered in the lake basin, these impacts will be of low magnitude and readily
manageable by known mitigation measures. Following the site-specific EMP to be developed
for the project, the project will be designed and installed with pollution control facilities and


                                                 VII
mitigation measures against noise, exhaust, wastewater and solid waste pollution. The project
will also implement fire prevention, pest management, and alien species control measures.
Environmental management training will be strengthened to ensure the implementation of daily
EMP implementation. Also, the project will support public education and enhance the
monitoring and management of traffic volume and visitor flow to prevent wildlife/habitat
destruction during project operation.

0.6 Environmental Management Plan
     The effective implementation of EMP is key to mitigate the above project-associated
negative impacts and ensure the achievements of anticipated environmental benefits as part of
the project objectives. As part of the EIA, an EMP (see Annex 1) has been developed to outline
the key environmental management requirements of the project. It includes the institutional
arrangements and responsibilities for environmental management, environmental mitigation
measures, monitoring and management measures during design, construction, and operation,
the environmental mitigation measures in the EIA and EMP will be incorporated into the
project design, bidding documents and construction contracts and will be implemented by the
design institutes, the contractors, and the PIUs under the supervision by the PMO and the local
ecology and environment authorities. The effectiveness of these measures will be assessed
based on the results of environmental inspections and monitoring to determine whether they
should be continued, improved or adjusted.

0.7 Stakeholder Engagement and Information Disclosure
     Making project information public and involving key stakeholders is essential for smooth
project implementation. Early stakeholder involvement in project design, decision-making,
implementation, monitoring and evaluation will ensure the project is well-designed and
implemented to avoid and minimize environmental risks and impacts by integrating the
stakeholders’ feedback. The stakeholders identified during project preparation include project
implementation agency, relevant governmental agencies, project-affected and other local
communities, vulnerable groups like farmers and small shopkeepers, ethnic minorities, and
local NGOs. A Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) has been developed to support the project
implementation.

     During project preparation, stakeholders were consulted along with the project's progress.
From October 2024 to February 2025, various municipal departments were consulted on the
initial project proposal, including Municipal Natural Resources Planning Bureau, Municipal


                                             VIII
Ecology and Environment Bureau, Municipal Water Authority, Municipal Traffic Management
Bureau, Municipal Forestry Bureau, through which strong supports and helpful feedbacks were
received in relation to further design improvements (locations and routing of proposed project
activities) and clarification of approval requirements from their own perspectives to support the
project preparation, for example, on woodland use, wetland park permission, etc. Also, the EIA
team gathered feedback from the communities in the project area through questionnaires and
consultation meetings, focusing on their potential environmental concerns in relation to project
construction and operation. The surveys revealed that: (i) The interviewed residents showed
overall supports to the project and future development of Aha Lake Basin after Aha Lake
reservoir was changed from the scope of drinking water source protection zone. In general,
they agreed with the proposed project siting and routing while recognizing the importance of
balancing local livelihood improvements versus ecological protection; (ii) for construction
period, their key environmental concerns are around the quality of surface water and local
ecology, the management of solid waste and traffic safety; while for operation period, the
environmental concerns are mainly about air pollution such as increased vehicle exhaust, traffic
noise and solid waste. In response to all the above feedback received, current FSR and
preliminary EIA has been improved to include corresponding activity adjustments and needed
mitigation measures. Per China’s EIA regulations and ESF requirements, the draft preliminary
EIA was disclosed locally at the official website of project implementing agency, namely,
Guiyang      Infrastructure     Construction        &   Investment       Group      Co.     Ltd.
(http://www.zggyct.com/gggs/ztbgg/fgcl/202503/t20250314_87176992.html) on Mar. 14th. The
DEIA was       disclosed   by   Guiyang    Municipal    Ecology    and   Environment      Bureau
(http://222.85.190.19:8204/xmspgy/xmsp/notice/advanceview?id=5201000094FXWZ2025043
0374479&type=NEW) on May 16th 2025. No feedback has been received so far.

0.8 Conclusions
     Based on the assessment conclusions, the project implementation is expected to bring
significant environmental and social benefits in relation to local biodiversity enhancement and
carbon emission reduction. Some of the project activities are located within the scope of Lake
Aha National Wetland Park and Guiyang’s delineated ecological redline; however, these
activities are designed in alignment with the local ecological conservation plan and national
regulations on ecological redline management and biodiversity protection. During construction
and operation, the project is anticipated to bring temporary and site-specific negative
environmental impacts, for example, construction nuisance, and increased traffic and so on. An


                                               IX
EMP has been prepared as part of current EIA to outline the mitigation measures to address
these negative environmental impacts. With the proposed mitigation measures taken, no
significant residual impacts are anticipated resulting from the project implementation.




                                               X
1 Overview

1.1 Project Background
     On March 28, 2023, the Guizhou Provincial People's Government approved and agreed to
cancel the centralized drinking water source protection zone of Aha Reservoir in Guiyang City.
The function of Aha Reservoir was adjusted from drinking water source to urban flood control
and ecological water replenishment. In the territorial spatial planning, "Lake Aha Green Heart"
was designated as the "one core (core of city building)" in the development pattern of "one core
and three centers". Accordingly, Lake Aha and the surrounding 100 km2 area are designated as
the Lake Aha area and are planned to be a pilot and demonstration area for the construction of
an ecologically civilized city.

     The study area of Guiyang Green Urban Development Project is the city of Guiyang, and
the construction project focuses on Lake Aha and its surrounding area, with the aim of
developing standards and demonstrating good practices to enhance the multiple uses of urban
forests, wetlands, and Lake Aha, such as reduction of carbon emissions, increase of carbon
sequestration, adoption of nature-based solutions to enhance resilience, and enhancement of
ecosystem services. This multi-use approach will provide methodologies, standards and
learning experiences that can be replicated in other cities in China and globally.




                           Figure 1-1 Planned Scope of the Lake Aha Area

                                                1
1.2 Purpose of the Project
     The construction objectives of the project are to reduce greenhouse gas emissions through
the implementation of green measures in urban areas, to increase carbon sequestration by
restoring ecosystem productivity, and to enhance the protection and sustainable management of
terrestrial areas and inland water areas for nature-positive urban development.

     Given that a single project cannot achieve all of Guiyang's nature-positive goals and
address all climate-related issues, this project uses Guiyang City's Lake Aha as a target area to
demonstrate an integrated approach to achieving these goals, complemented by low-carbon
platforms, systems, policies, research, and fundamental monitoring and evaluation activities
that encompass the entire city of Guiyang.

1.3 Project Description
1.3.1 Construction contents
     The design of the project framework incorporates the lessons learned from the Bank's
previous projects in China, emphasizing the combination of "physical" (infrastructure) and
"non-physical" (technical assistance) activities. The project construction contents are divided
into three aspects: low carbon planning system and research, construction of a low-carbon and
nature-positive city demonstration area in Lake Aha, and project management and capacity
building, with specific construction contents and scale as follows:

     Subcomponent 1: Low-carbon planning, systems and research. This sub-project will
lay the groundwork for establishing Guiyang as a national, regional and global city of good
practice in monitoring urban carbon emissions and reducing emissions by incorporating the
concepts of low carbon and nature positive in urban spatial planning, supporting research on
carbon sequestration and its methodology, and supporting carbon market financing. The
subcomponent consists of four sub-activities

     - sub-activity 1.1: Guiyang low-carbon smart platform and green account.

     Green Account Management: Based on the research results of Guiyang City's Green
Account, the Green Account Management Platform of Guiyang City will be set up to provide
carbon emission management services for individuals, enterprises and the government through
the data of users' low-carbon behaviors. Green Transportation and Low-Carbon Publicity,
combining Guiyang City's urban transportation information system to guide urban
transportation and improve the safety of the transportation system; meanwhile, it will carry out


                                                2
publicity activities such as World Earth Day, World Environment Day, National Energy
Conservation Awareness Week, National Low-Carbon Day, and Guizhou Ecology Day.

     Low-carbon smart service integrated management platform, relying on Guiyang city's
state-owned medical, education, smart parking, advertising and media content, integration of
government affairs and livelihood services, to gradually realize the sharing of information and
digitization of high-quality assets among various platforms, and provide the public with
efficient, convenient and high-quality one-stop services integrating government, people, and
business at the same time while realizing the operation and management of asset digitization,
so as to realize low-carbon, smart and digitized synergistic integration of governmental
resources and social resources. It will realize the synergistic integration of government
resources and social resources in a low-carbon, smart and digital way.

     -     sub-activity 1.2: Climate-positive urban spatial planning systems.

     Utilizing the Green Urban Development Project as an opportunity to focus on Lake Aha and
expand to the whole city, to study the effective path for reducing emissions and increasing carbon sinks
from the perspective of spatial planning, provide new ideas for the ecological construction of Guiyang
City, and form a "1+3" low-carbon city research system, where "1" refers to the low-carbon city special
plan, and "3" refers to three special supporting studies.

     -     sub-activity 1.3: Carbon sequestration methodological studies.

     Combined with the work foundation of the karst carbon sink project, study and formulate the "Karst
Carbon Sinks of Greenhouse Gas (GHG) Voluntary Emission Reduction Project Methodology" in strict
accordance with the requirements for the development of GHG voluntary emission reduction projects,
select typical karst geomorphological regions within and outside the province to carry out evaluation and
verification of the applicability of the methodology, carry out field monitoring, sampling and analysis,
and accounting of the results on a regular basis, and optimize the methodology based on the results of the
testing and analysis, and the design documents of GHG voluntary emission reduction project will be
prepared in accordance with the methodology requirements, so as to form a complete set of information
for the declaration of the methodology of the GHG voluntary reduction project to the state and strive to
promote it to become a national methodology.

     -     sub-activity 1.4: Mid-term and long-term low-carbon and nature-positive urban
development models and feasibility studies.




                                                     3
     Subcomponent 2: Lake Aha low-carbon and nature-positive urban demonstration area.
Demonstration activities carried out under this sub-project focus on Lake Aha and its surrounding area,
as well as the wider water area and transportation system associated with the area. The subcomponent
includes four sub-activities:

     -     sub-activity 2.1: Restore and improve urban green spaces, habitats and ecosystems.

     Aimed at restoring local ecosystems for multiple benefits, including increased carbon sequestration
(by enhancing the function and capacity of urban forests, wetlands and water bodies), the sub-activity
also includes studies on monitoring, assessment and conservation of biodiversity. The main construction
elements are summarized in Table 1.3-1.

      sub-activity 2.3: Enhancing green urban transportation.

     This sub-activity includes the development of a non-motorized transport network around Lake Aha,
the enhancement of the public transport system and the improvement of the urban road network to
reduce congestion. Based on Guiyang's ecotourism development model, the construction of a greenway
around Lake Aha will improve the quality of life in the city by providing access to the lake for citizens
and tourists. Guiyang's urban transportation system will be improved by rehabilitating roads in and out of
the Lake Aha area to ease regional traffic congestion, improve travel efficiency, and reduce greenhouse
gas emissions by improving fuel efficiency. It aims to reduce carbon emissions from the transportation
sector and promote green urban transportation.

     -    sub-activity 2.4: Other public infrastructure and low-carbon lifestyles.

     Project activities include improving the energy efficiency of the Lake Aha water supply system,

1.3.2 Construction sites
    The scope of the technical assistance study for this project covers the entire city of
Guiyang, while the civil works project is mainly located in the Lake Aha planning area. The
Lake Aha planning area is bounded on the east by the Lake Aha National Wetland Park
boundary and the West Second Ring Road, on the south by Gui'an Avenue and Tianhetan
Avenue, on the west by Guantan Avenue, and on the north by the Taijin Line.




                                               11
                                Figure 1-2 Project Location Map

1.4 Preparation of the Domestic Environmental Impact Assessment (DEIA)
     According to the requirements of the World Bank's Environmental and Social Framework
(ESF), a comprehensive DEIA should be conducted, public participation and information
disclosure will be carried out, and a corresponding environmental management plan (included
as an annex to the EIA document) will be prepared to provide guidance for the environmental
management of the Project.

     At the same time, according to the "Classified Management List of Environmental Impact
Assessment of Construction Projects" (2021 Edition), taking into account the construction
content of the project and the sensitive areas, it is determined that the domestic procedure for
this project needs to prepare a report form for environmental impact assessment of construction
projects, and submit it to Guiyang Municipal Ecology and Environment Bureau for approval.
Currently, the DEIA of the project has been approved by Guiyang Municipal Ecology and
                                              12
Environment Bureau in May 2025 (including special ecological assessment and special
acoustic environmental assessment).

1.4.1 Objectives and principles of environmental assessment
        The main objectives of this environmental assessment include:

        •   Identify and assess all relevant, direct, indirect and cumulative environmental and
ecological risks and impacts, both favorable and unfavorable, over the life of the project;

        •   Ensure that environmental and ecological risks and impacts of the project are
identified, avoided, minimized, mitigated or alleviated;

        •   Avoid negative environmental impacts and, and where they are not avoidable, take
measures to minimize, mitigate, remedy, offset and even compensate for them; and at the same
time, benefit the environment and the community as much as possible;

        •   Ensure that affected communities are involved in the assessment process in an
appropriate form in relation to the issues that may affect them;

        •   Drive project management and improve environmental performance through effective
use of Environmental Management Plan (EMP) and Biodiversity Management Plan (BMP),
etc.;

        •   Integrate Chinese laws and regulations, standards, and requirements, and the World
Bank's Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) and EHS Guidelines into environmental
assessment and corresponding management plans.

1.4.2 Assessment process
      The environmental assessment flowchart is available atFigure , and the main steps are
listed below:




                                                13
                                    Figure 1-3 EIA Flowchart

（1） Data collection

    Gather information related to the project and understand the various regulations, policies
and standards that should be implemented for the project to ensure that all the following
relevant information can be provided when carrying out the environmental assessment:

       Results of previous biodiversity surveys;

       Project feasibility studies and design plans;

       EIA report form for the project (special ecological assessment report, special acoustic
environmental assessment report);
                                               14
       Status of the ecosystem in the project area (especially in Lake Aha Wetland Park);

       Key findings of the dam safety assessment;

       Report on the assessment of the ecological impact of the construction project on the
National Wetland Park;

       Project soil and water conservation plan;

       Information on the project's justification on flood discharge capacity;

       Other matters to be included, such as issues raised by potentially affected populations.

（2） Current status study

    •   On October 24 and November 14, 2024, the consultant team conducted an on-site
         survey.

    •   From November 15, 2024, to present, information has been collected and analyzed,
         such as project construction documents and plans, ecological zoning control plans,
         environmentally sensitive areas, and related information such as ecological sample lot
         and line surveys, acoustic/water baseline monitoring data, map of vegetation types in
         the project area, and maps of the current land use.

（3） Stakeholder consultation and public participation

    Research on the current state of the environment within the project's scope of impact. The
investigation of the current state of the environment is mainly based on the collection of
existing information, combined with visits to relevant government departments, site visits and
household surveys (community interviews).

    •   On October 23-24, 2024, the consultant team discussed with the PMO, the design
         team, and the Committee on Ecology, Environment, and Ethnic and Religious Affairs
         on the domestic environmental requirements, the requirements of the Bank's
         Environmental and Social Framework (ESF), and the preparation of the
         environmental and social documents.

    •   On November 13-14, 2024, the consultant team communicated with the PMO, the
         design team, and the Lake Aha Dam Management Office on environmental and social
         issues. Discussions were held to understand the contents of the project and the
         upstream and downstream services involved to identify potential environmental


                                               15
         impacts during project implementation, the status of the wastewater treatment
         facilities on which the project's interception works will be based, and associated
         facilities.

     •   On December 5, 2024, the consultant team confirmed with the FSR consultant and the
         Wetland Park Management Office online regarding the environmental management
         requirements of the National Wetland Park Conservation Area and discussed the
         feasibility of activities under the project.

     •   On December 11, 2024, there was an on-line discussion with the PMO, the FSR
         consultant, and the ecology and environment department to discuss whether the
         project involves dredging activities and whether it involves specialized forestry
         activities. The ecology and environment department mentioned (1) the issue of buffer
         zone delineation in the Lake Aha basin, and coordination between project
         construction and environmental response planning to be considered; (2) emphasis on
         the protection of bird habitat and the role of agricultural land in biodiversity
         conservation.

     •   December 2024-January 2025, communicated with the FSR consultant and the PMO
         regarding the need for special ecological assessment report for activities that involves
         national key terrestrial wildlife habitat, which should be included in the DEIA report,
         and the opinions from the forestry department should be sought during the process of
         DEIA report approval.

（4） Impact assessment and mitigation measures

     Potential environmental impacts identified are assessed by quantitative or qualitative
methods. The magnitude of the impact depends on the severity of the impact and the sensitivity
of the receptor. The size of the impacts assessed determines whether additional mitigation
measures and management systems need to be added. If the remaining impacts are significant,
another assessment is required.

（5） Environmental Management Plan

     An Environmental Management Plan (EMP) will be included in the DEIA report. The
EMP translates the environmental mitigation measures identified in the report into a series of
specific requirements that are actionable for construction contractors, operators, and managers,



                                                 16
each of which has a responsible person, timeframe for completion, and monitoring
requirements.

1.5 Scope and Factors of Assessment
1.5.1 Preliminary identification of environmental impacts
     The project can be broadly categorized into infrastructure, ecological restoration and
protection, and technical assistance according to the contents of the activities. The physical
investments include the construction of new roads and wastewater networks, while the
ecological restoration and protection category mainly includes various types of restoration
projects such as forests and wetlands; the technical assistance category includes program and
methodology research, scientific research and monitoring, and training.

     Combined with the contents, scale, operation mode and environmental characteristics of
activities, the matrix method is used to carry out preliminary identification and analysis of the
possible impacts of the project activities on each environmental factor, and the results are
shown in Table 1.5-1 and Table 1.5-2.

     The project is divided into design, construction and operation phases. The design phase
can reduce the environmental impacts of project implementation by optimizing siting and
routing, ecological restoration methods, species selection, etc., but the design activities
themselves have little or no impact on the environment and are not analyzed here. The
construction phase is mainly the construction phase of the project activities, such as road
construction, and the process of planting/cutting down vegetation during the construction of
cycling stations and interception pipeline network, and habitat restoration activities. The
operation period includes roads, wastewater pump stations, activities of visitors of greenway
and stations, vegetation maintenance phase of ecological restoration activities, observation of
biodiversity, and tourism education.

                                                      18
     The project will target existing water quality pollution, ecological destruction of wetlands,
forest land destruction, etc. for interception of wastewater and water pollution control,
ecological restoration, vegetation restoration on forest land and construction of ecological
corridors to promote biodiversity protection and enhancement.

     Through the preliminary identification of impacts, it can be seen that the construction
period of the project will produce certain negative impacts, mainly including dust, noise,
destruction of vegetation, disturbance to animals, etc., while the operation period, although
there may still be certain negative environmental impacts, such as the operation of the cycling
stations, visitor service centers and other operations to produce three wastes, road vehicle
exhaust, noise, etc., mainly positive impacts will show up in general and especially in terms of
ecology, which is conducive to the protection and upgrade of animals, vegetation, habitats,
diversity and other ecological factors.

1.5.2 Categories and priorities of assessment
     Following the World Bank's Environmental Social Framework (ESF) policy, the
environmental and social risk rating of projects can be categorized into four levels: high,
substantial, moderate, and low, which follow the definitions below:

                 Table 0-2 Guidelines for Environmental and Social Risk Categories

  hierarchy                                                criteria
                Project activities may generate significant environmental and social risks and adverse
                impacts of various types due to their complexity, scale or sensitive location, and some of
                the environmental and social impacts of the project may not be effectively mitigated
    High
                through measures, or the mitigation measures may be difficult to implement because of the
                potential for serious social conflict or risks to human security, or because of capacity
                constraints in the Borrower State or on the part of the project participants.
                The project may have significant environmental and social risks/impacts, but the level of
                complexity or environmental-social risk is expected to be lower than for high-risk projects,
 Substantial
                and impacts can be reduced to acceptable levels through the implementation of specific
                mitigation measures.
                The potential environmental and social risks and adverse impacts of the project are not
  Moderate      significant, are easily predictable, and can be effectively avoided or controlled through the
                implementation of conventional mitigation measures.
                Environmental and social impacts are generally minor, or negligible and no further
    Low
                mitigation measures are required.

     It is usually necessary to determine the risk category of a project by taking into account
the nature, scale, severity of environmental and social impacts, scope of impacts, duration, and
management capacity of the project implementation entity.

     According to the results of the preliminary identification of the environmental impacts of

                                                    19
the project, the project as a whole is conducive to the improvement of regional environmental
quality, ecological environment protection and biodiversity enhancement. However, part of the
project requires construction operations in the National Wetland Park, which may have certain
negative ecological impacts on wildlife and habitats; earth moving construction may
exacerbate soil erosion, and there is a risk of pests, diseases, and forest fires. Pollutants such as
particulate matter, wastewater, noise and solid waste may be generated during implementation,
which may cause occupational health and safety impacts on construction or staff. Traffic noise,
automobile exhaust, etc. during the operation period of the project, tourists' domestic
wastewater, domestic garbage, etc will be generated.

     The negative environmental impacts generated by this project are mainly short-term
impacts generated during the construction period, which can be reduced to an acceptable level
by adopting specific mitigation measures; during the operation period, only some of the
activities will generate environmental impacts along with the production and operation,
excursion, and other activities, and their impacts are small in magnitude and scope, which can
be effectively avoided or controlled by adopting mitigation measures.

     Considering the above factors, the environmental risk level of this project is
"Substantial", although the project may generate significant environmental impacts, the
impacts can be reduced to an acceptable level through the adoption of appropriate measures.

1.5.3 Scope of assessment
     The scope of the assessment was determined primarily by reference to the following
documents:

        Technical Guidelines for the Preparation of Environmental Impact Report Forms for
          Construction Projects (Pollution Impact Category) (Trial)

        Technical Guidelines for the Preparation of Environmental Impact Report Forms for
          Construction Projects (Ecological Impact Category) (for Trial Implementation), No.
          33, EIA [2020] of the EIA Office of the Government of the PRC.

        Technical Guidelines for Environmental Impact Assessment Ecological Impact
          (HJ19-2022)

        Technical Guidelines on Environmental Impact Assessment for Surface Water
          Environment (HJ2.3-2018)



                                                 20
        Technical Guidelines for Environmental Impact Assessment on Acoustic Environment
           (HJ2.4-2021)

        World Bank Environmental and Social Framework

（1） Ecological environment

     The project construction period mainly poses a short-term negative impact on the
ecological environment, which is geographically limited, the direct impact range is the scope of
the project occupation, and the indirect impacts are mainly exhaust gas, wastewater, noise
emissions on the surrounding ecological environment. According to the planning of Lake Aha
and the construction content of the existing project, it is initially determined that the ecological
impact assessment level in the DEIA of the project is “Grade 1”, and the scope of assessment is
the overlapping area of 300m outside the red line of the entire Lake Aha Wetland Park and
300m outside the construction area of the Wetland Park, and the scope of the investigation can
be appropriately expanded if there are important habitats of important species outside the range
of 300m.

     The impact on the ecological environment during the operation period of the project is
mainly positive and long-term, and the scope of assessment considers the ecological units
involved in the project's occupation range.

（2） Atmospheric environment

     The exhaust pollutants generated during the construction and operation periods of the
project are basically in the form of unorganized emissions, which only have an impact on the
proximity, among which the impact range of the major pollutant, construction dust, is generally
within 200m downwind of the construction site. Therefore, the scope of atmospheric
environment impact assessment is set at 200m outside the boundary of the project site.

（3） Surface water environment

     The wastewater discharge of the project is basically construction wastewater and domestic
wastewater, which is treated by self-built integrated wastewater treatment facilities, septic
tanks and other existing treatment facilities and then reused for irrigation, landscaping,
sprinkling and so on, and is not directly discharged to surface water bodies. During the
operation period of the rural water pollution prevention and control project in Baiyan River and
Youyu River basins, domestic wastewater is treated by wastewater treatment facilities and then
used for agricultural irrigation and is not directly discharged into water bodies. The wastewater

                                                21
from the interceptor project is lifted through pump station upgraded and eventually treated in
Erqiao Wastewater Treatment Plant and Xiaohe Wastewater Treatment Plant to meet the
standards and then discharged. However, considering the environmental risk factors of
water-related construction and operation during the construction period, Lake Aha is taken as
the scope of environmental impact assessment for surface water.

（4） Acoustic environment

     During the construction period of the project, the major impacts are construction activities
on the surrounding residents and material transportation on the residents along the road, as well
as noise generated by the operation of pump station equipment and vehicle driving during the
operation period. With reference to the DEIA, the scope of the acoustic environmental impact
assessment is 200m outside the boundary of the construction zone, and 200m on both sides of
the centerline of the road during the operation period.

1.5.4 Assessment factors
     Based on the identification of environmental impact factors, combined with the project
characteristics and the current level of environmental quality, the assessment factors of the
project are determined and divided into two categories: ecology and environment.

（1） Ecological impact assessment factors

     Ecology is mainly assessed qualitatively and quantitatively in terms of the distribution
range and population size of species; the quality, area and connectivity of habitats; the species
composition and community structure of biomes; the vegetation cover, biomass and ecosystem
functions of ecosystems; the main protection objects and ecological functions of ecologically
sensitive areas; and soil erosion.

（2） Environmental assessment factors

     The environment mainly involves in terms of discharge of exhaust, wastewater, and noise,
as well as the disposal of solid waste.

        Exhaust mainly involves SO2, NO2, particulate matter, CO, with air quality standards
and O3, Carbon emissions involve greenhouse gas CO2.

        Wastewater is analyzed for discharge compliance only.

        Acoustic environment mainly involves the impacts of construction and transportation
activities as well as operational activities on sensitive points.

                                                  22
        Solid waste mainly involves spoil of construction excavation, abandoned pipes from
water supply pipe network expansion and domestic garbage.

        The project essentially does not contaminate soil or groundwater and is only analyzed
in a simple qualitative manner.

     The assessment factors for this project are as follows:

ESS1, ESS2, ESS3, ESS4, ESS6, ESS8, and ESS10, as detailed in the Table 2.2-1.

2.3 World Bank’s Environment, Health and Safety Guidelines (EHSGs)
      The World Bank's Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) requires projects to
consider the IFC’s Environment, Health and Safety Guidelines (EHSGs) and international good
industry practices during implementation. Currently, the EHSGs consist of 1 general guideline


                                               15
and 62 sectoral guidelines. This project applies the general guidelines and the EHS Guidelines
for Water and Sanitation and the EHS Guidelines for the Forest Harvesting Operations.

2.3.1 General Environment, Health, and Safety Guidelines
     Effective management of EHS issues requires that EHS considerations be factored into the
management process at the enterprise and facility, and that this be done in an organized,
hierarchical manner that includes the following steps:

         Identify potential EHS risks and hazards early in the preparatory phase of project
construction, including consideration of EHS influences in site selection, planning, design, and
construction documents.

         Involvement of professionals who assess and manage EHS impacts and risks in the
relevant work, including the use of techniques recommended in the Guidelines as applicable to
the project when preparing plans and procedures for the project or specific operational
activities.

         Understand the likelihood of EHS risks and the severity of the consequences:

         The nature of the project activity, e.g. whether the project will use pesticides and
whether there is a risk of leakage during storage and transportation. Whether there is a risk of
forest fires during construction and operation of the project, etc.

         Potential impacts on employees, the community or the environment if risk prevention
measures are not taken. As a result, the project management or operating organization or
facility should prepare an emergency response plan and conduct regular drills.

         Prioritize risk management strategies to achieve an overall reduction in risks to human
health and environment, with a focus on preventing irreversible and/or significant impacts.

         Prioritize strategies to eliminate hazards or risk factors at source, e.g., selecting
pesticides, pesticide products or formulations that comply with the EHS Guidelines, adopting
bio-extermination techniques, etc.

         If environmental and social impacts are still unavoidable, the impacts on the
environment and society are reduced through engineering and management measures, such as
the use of pollution control measures to reduce the level of pollutant emissions.




                                                 16
            Continuous monitoring of the environmental performance of a business or facility and
pollutant outlets, along with effective and efficient accountability, leads to improved EHS
performance.

         The guidelines also include general control measures and monitoring requirements for
wastewater, exhaust, solid waste and noise. The requirements of the guidelines are applicable
to the environmental management and occupational health and safety management of the
activities of the project.

2.3.2 Environment, Health, and Safety Guidelines for Forest Harvesting Operations
         The guidelines are applicable to the forest conservation and harvesting activities of the
various ecological restoration subcomponents of the project. The guidelines contain
information on the management of planted and natural forests in temperate, boreal and tropical
regions1 .

2.3.3 Environment, Health, and Safety Guidelines for Water and Sanitation
         The wastewater interception under the project, which includes the collection of
wastewaters through a centralized system (e.g., a piped sewer collection network) and the
treatment of the collected wastewater at a centralized facility, shall be subject to the
requirements of the guidelines. The guidelines contain information on potable water treatment
and distribution systems and the collection of wastewater through a centralized system or a
decentralized system and the treatment of the collected wastewater at a centralized facility.

2.3.4 Environmental, Health, and Safety Guidelines for Waste Management Facilities
         The construction and operation phases of the project involve the collection and disposal of
construction waste and domestic waste. The guidelines shall be applicable to this project. The
guidelines cover various facilities or projects specifically designed to manage municipal solid
waste and industrial waste, including waste collection and transportation, waste acceptance,
unloading, treatment and storage.

2.4 Assessment Standards
         The project will implement more stringent standards based on a comparison between
Chinese standards and relevant WB standards applicable to the project.

                            Alternanthera philoxeroides, etc.) to grasp their invasive species, population
                            abundance, main distribution areas, etc., and take preventive and control

                            removing them artificially, and using a mower to make clear of the larger
                            scale invasive alien plants, without using herbicides and other chemical
                            methods. Synchronized biological prevention and control research will be

         The study area for this project is the city of Guiyang, and the construction activities are
primarily located in the Lake Aha planning area. The project plan location is shown in the
following figure.




                                      Figure 3-1 Project Layout

3.3 Identification of Environmental Risks and Impacts
3.3.1 Policy Risks
     (i) Conservation and utilization planning in forestry


                                                   26
     The project will occupy Class I forest land in Huaxi District and Yunyan District of
Guiyang City, and the occupation is shown in the following figure. According to the State
Forestry Administration Decree No. 35 and the Notice of Guizhou Forestry Bureau on the
Implementation of "Management Norms for the Examination and Approval of the Use of
Forest Land for Construction Projects" (Guizhou Forestry Fa [2022] No. 16), the forest land
protection and utilization plan needs to be adjusted for this project, and then the formalities for
the use of forest land can be carried out.

     The project has gained the Approval on the Adjustment of Forest Land Protection Level in
the Areas around Lake Aha Reservoir in Guiyang City (HUAFUHAN [2025] No.29) issued by
Huaxi District People’s Government, and the Approval on the Adjustment of Class I Forest
Land Level in the Centralized Drinking Water Source Protection Zone at Lake Aha Reservoir
of Guiyang City issued by Yunyan District People’s Government on April 3rd 2025, and the
Class I forest land in the project area has been adjusted to Class II and III forest land.




                   Figure 3-2 Relationship of Construction Activities with Forest Land

                                                 27
    (ii) Compliance analysis with the Wetlands Protection Law and the Management
Methods of National Nature Parks

    Some of the construction activities under the project are located in Lake Aha National
Wetland Park, and according to the "Wetland Protection Law of the People's Republic of
China" and “National Nature Park Management Methods (Trial)”, the project construction shall
seek the opinions from Guiyang Lake Aha Wetland Park Management Office under the
National Park Management Department and the provincial forestry authority.

    This project has gained the Letter of Feedback on the Site Selection in Lake Aha National
Wetland Park of Guiyang City, Guizhou Province for Guiyang Green Urban Development
Project issued by Guizhou Provincial Forestry Department on April 16th 2025, and the Reply
Comments on the Occupation of Lake Aha National Wetland Park of Guiyang City by Guiyang
Green Urban Development Project issued by Guiyang Lake Aha Wetland Park Management
Office on April 18th 2025, where both Guiyang Lake Aha Wetland Park Management Office
and Guizhou Provincial Forestry Department approved the project’s site selection.




               Figure 3-3 Relationship of Construction Activities with the Wetland Park

                                               28
     (iii) Compliance analysis with the three zones and three lines

     According to the results of the superimposed map of "three zones and three lines", the
project involves 446.90mu of the ecological protection red line. According to the Notice on
Strengthening the Management of Ecological Protection Red Line issued by the Ministry of
Natural Resources, the Ministry of Ecology and Environment, and the National Forestry and
Grassland Administration (Trial) (ZIRANZIFA [2022] No.142) and the Measures for the
Supervision of the Red Line of Ecological Protection of Guizhou Province (Trial), only limited
human activities are allowed in the area outside the core protection zone of the nature reserves
within the ecological protection red line under the premise of compliance with the laws and
regulations.

     This project has gained the Letter of Review Comments on the Compliance of Permitted
Limited Human Activities within the Ecological Protection Red Line involved under Guiyang
Green Urban Development Project on April 23rd 2025, where the project proposal was
approved.




 Figure 3-4 Relationship between the Construction Activities and the Ecological Protection Red Line

                                                29
     (iv) Compliance analysis with the Wildlife Protection Law

     According to the announcement of the State Forestry and Grassland Administration (No.
23 of 2023) (List of Important Habitats for Terrestrial Wildlife (First Batch)), Lake Aha
National Wetland Park in Guiyang, Guizhou, was designated by the State Forestry and
Grassland Administration as one of the first 789 important habitats for wildlife in January 2024.
According to the Law of the People's Republic of China on the Protection of Wild Animals, the
opinion of the wildlife protection authorities of the people's governments of the provinces,
autonomous regions and municipalities directly under the central government shall be sought
for the project.

     This project has gained the Letter of Feedback on the Site Selection within the Key
Habitat of Terrestrial Wildlife for Guiyang Green Urban Development Project issued by
Guizhou Provincial Forestry Department on April 27th 2025, where the site selection of the
project was approved.

                                                                         31
3.3.2 Environmental risk identification
     Part of the project are research, management platform development and institutional
capacity building as technical assistance activities, and the project itself and downstream
activities are free of environmental and social risks. On the other hand, the construction of
greenway, interceptor pipelines and transportation facilities such as roads, bus terminals,
parking lots, etc. around Lake Aha will require the occupation of ecological protection red lines
and important habitats, which will bring about impacts to the surrounding ecological
environment and the production and life of the community residents. The project
environmental and social team has identified the main potential social risks of the project.
According to the results of the project's risk identification (see Table 3.3-2 for details), the
project's comprehensive risk rating is “Substantial”. This report only provides a detailed
analysis of the environmental impacts of the project, and the analysis of the project's social
impacts is reflected in the project's social impact assessment report.

     The environmental impacts of the project construction are summarized as follows: (1) The
greenway and access routes, C416 upgrading and the lake interception ditch occupy a total of
446.90mu of the ecological protection red line, and the occupation of the red line by the
construction has caused destruction of the vegetation and disturbance to the surrounding
animals. (2) Wastewater, waste and noise during the construction phase of the transportation
project and rural water pollution control project cause disturbance to the surrounding residents,
and noise during the operation phase of the road project affects the residents on both sides of
the road. (3) Soil erosion caused by excavation during the construction phase of the project,
and unfavorable traffic organization during the construction period may affect the travel of the
surrounding residents. However, the project construction also has obvious positive
environmental and social benefits: (1) The wetland restoration at the lake inlets, water
ecological restoration, shoreline restoration, bird habitat restoration and the construction of
ecological corridors, etc., can improve the quality of the ecosystem of the project area and
mitigate and compensate for the negative impacts arising from the construction of the project.
(2) In addition, the PMO and local government have rich experience in project management
and strong institutional capacity.

     Therefore, by combining the project activities, the sensitivity of the project area, and the
implementation capacity of the project management organization, the environmental risk of the
project is finally determined to be “Substantial”.

3.4 Identification of Associated Facilities
     The ESF defines an Associated Facility as a facility or activity that is not financed as part
of the project, but (a) is directly and substantially related to the project; (b) is carried out, or is
planned to be carried out, concurrently with the project; and (c) is necessary for the feasibility
of the project and would not have been constructed, expanded, or carried out in the absence of
the proposed project.

     The project has been analyzed, and no associated facilities are involved.

3.5 Environmental Lifting and Dependable Facilities
3.5.1 Status of wastewater treatment in the project area
     Wastewater from Lake Aha mainly comes from around the lake, including the Jinzhu area
in the south, the Jiu’an area in the west, the Aha Village area in the east and the Caoba area in
the north. The current regional wastewater treatment rate is about 50%, and the
centralized treatment rate is about 30%.

     In view of the various problems existing in the current situation, this project will carry out
water pollution control in some villages of Baiyan River and Youyu River basins, wastewater
interception, dredging, separation of rainwater and wastewater, and river regulation of Lanni
Gully basin, and upgrading of interception of Xiaoche River basin.

3.5.2 Analysis of dependable wastewater treatment plants
     The upstream wastewater treatment plants within the Aha Reservoir basin are the Jinyang
Wastewater Treatment Plant and the Shiban Township Wastewater Treatment Plant in Huaxi
District, and the wastewater treatment stations are mainly located in the Baiyan River, Youyu
River, Caichong Gully, and Lanni Gully basins, as well as around Lake Aha. The WWTPs
downstream within the Aha Reservoir basin include Erqiao WWTP and Xiaohe WWTP, which
are the WWTPs that the interception works of the project need to be lifted to and dependent on.
A diagram of the relationship between the project activities and the dependable WWTPs is

                                                   45
4 Environmental Baselines

4.1 Status of the Regional Natural Environment
4.1.1 Geographical location and scope
     The study area of the project is located in Guiyang City, and the construction projects are
mainly located in the southwestern part of Guiyang city center, involving six districts, namely
Huaxi District, Nanming District, Yunyan District, Jingkai District, Guanshanhu District, and
Gui’an New District. Most of the projects are located in Lake Aha National Wetland Park.

4.1.2 Topography
     The project is built around Lake Aha, which is located in the area of karst geomorphology
and normal geomorphology intertwined as the main pattern. The peaks and hills in the lake
area are typical conical karst hills, interlaced with the valley and the mountains are huge and
rounded, and there are a large number of scattered islands in the lake, and the more widely
distributed are carbonate rocks. The overall terrain is high in the west and low in the east, high
in the north and low in the south, with rolling mountain ranges in the west and north, and flatter
terrain in the east. Most of the elevation is 1100~1250m, and the relative height of the lake area
is 30~150m. The geomorphology along the route is greatly affected by the lithology and
tectonics, and the exposed strata are mainly Triassic limestone, dolomite, Permian sandstone,
mudstone and shale, which are strongly weathered by wind and eroded by flowing water, and
the dissolution of the carbonate zone is serious, and the karst is more developed, and the
geomorphic type is dominated by the geomorphic units with dissolution-erosion.

4.1.3 Climatic conditions
     The project area belongs to the north subtropical, where the climate in winter and spring is
semiarid and humid in summer, there is no severe cold in winter and no intense heat in summer,
the four seasons are distinctive, the average annual temperature is 15.3 ℃, the coldest month is
January with an average of 4.9 ℃, the hottest month is July with an average of 24.0 ℃, the
highest extreme used to be 39.5 ℃, the lowest extreme used to be -7.8 ℃, and the average
annual precipitation is 1174.7 mm, which is concentrated in the second half of the year; the
average annual wind speed is 2.2m/s, dominated by NE wind throughout the year, while S
wind prevails in summer and N wind in winter, the number of days with wind >8 degree is 8
days, the frequency of static wind is 38%, the gale with a return period of one in 30 years is
21.9m/s, and the average number of gale (≥8) per year is 11.6 days, which results in a large
wind load. The annual average relative humidity is 77%, the annual sunshine is 1420.0h, the



                                                 46
annual snow depth is up to 8cm, the annual frost-free period is 261 days, and the annual
average number of fog days is 9.1 days. Rainfall is mainly concentrated in summer and fall.

4.1.4 Soil
     The area under the jurisdiction of Guiyang City is characterized by a variety of soil types,
with the main soil-forming parent rocks being carbonate rocks, weathered clastic rocks and red
clay of the Quaternary period. There are 6 soil classes including loam, limestone soil, purple
soil, marsh soil, tidal soil and rice soil, 18 subclasses, 51 soil genera and 100 soil species. The
soil-forming parent rock in Lake Aha Wetland Park is dominated by carbonate rock, and the
soil type is dominated by yellow loam, limestone soil, marsh soil, with a small amount of rice
soil distributed occasionally.

4.1.5 Hydrology
     (i) Surface water

     The project area belongs to the Wujiang River system of the Yangtze River Basin, the
main lake is Lake Aha, and the catchment area upstream the dam site of Aha Reservoir is about
190 square kilometers, and the basin consists of five tributaries into the reservoir: Youyu River,
Baiyan River, Caichong River, Jinzhong River (Xiaowan River), and Lannigou River, which
are the second-level tributaries of the Nanming River of the Wujiang River system of the
Yangtze River Basin. Among them, the Youyu River, Baiyan River and Caichong River are
larger, and their soil erosion is relatively heavier. The characteristics of the main tributaries
into the reservoir are shown in the table. The distribution of the water system is shown in the
following figure.

                 Table 4.1-1 List of Characteristics of the Main Rivers into Lake Aha

                   Figure 4-1 Distribution of Water Systems in the Lake Aha Basin

     Before March year 2023, Aha Reservoir used to be the centralized drinking water source
of Guiyang City, and the water quality of Aha Reservoir was subject to the standard of
Category III of Lake Reservoir in "Surface Water Environmental Quality Standard"
(GB3838-2002). The target water quality will remain unchanged after the abolition of the
protection zone.

     (ii) Groundwater

     According to the stratigraphic lithology, characteristics of water-bearing media and
groundwater dynamics in the region, the main types of groundwater in the region are loose
rock pore water and karst fissure water. The main source of groundwater replenishment in the
region is atmospheric precipitation, and the replenishment mode is surface replenishment.
Precipitation is replenished through dissolution fissures, interlayer fissures and tectonic fissures.
According to the hydrogeological data of the region, the surrounding Aha Reservoir is the
groundwater discharge datum, and the groundwater level in the region is about 1126 meters,
with the depth of groundwater ranging from 8 to 23 meters. The area is a groundwater




                                                  48
replenishment and runoff area, with springs exposed, and under the influence of the regional
geological structure and karst, the hydrogeological conditions of the site are complicated.

4.2 Regional Socio-economic Status
4.2.1 Administrative divisions and population profile
        Guiyang, abbreviated as "Zhu", is located in the central part of Guizhou Province, the
capital of Guizhou Province, and is the center of the province's politics, economy, culture,
science and technology, and information. The city has 6 districts, 1 city and 3 counties under its
jurisdiction, with a land area of 8043.45 square kilometers. In 2023, the city's year-end resident
population was 6,402,900, an increase of 2.9% over the previous year; the average annual
population was 6,311,700, an increase of 2.4%. Guiyang is a multi-ethnic provincial capital city,
with 55 ethnic groups in the city, including Han, Miao, Buyi, Tujia, Yi, Dong, Gelao, Bai, Hui,
Manchu, Zhuang, Shui, Mongol, Li and Yao, including 11 hereditary ethnic minorities, with
Miao and Buyi as the main ones. There are 18 ethnic townships and 279 villages, and 228
villages inhabited by ethnic minorities. Data from the seventh population census shows that
Guiyang City had a resident population of 5.987 million in 2020, of which 1.2833 million were
ethnic minorities, accounting for 21.44% of the city's total population, and the percentage of
ethnic minority population is significantly higher than the national average of 8.89%. The
project's social impact assessment team conducted field surveys between November and
December 2024 in the villages where the project's land acquisition and resettlement will take
place. According to the results of the survey2, the villages affected by the project's land
acquisition and resettlement, such as Zhulin Village, Jinshan Village, Lanni Village, and
Baishao Village, have a larger population of ethnic minorities, and also have a higher
percentage. The ethnic minorities in these villages mainly live around Lake Aha and are
dominated by the Buyi and Miao ethnic groups. These ethnic minorities are immigrants who
were relocated and resettled from the reservoir flooded area during the construction of Aha
Reservoir in 1958. The ethnic minority population in the affected villages is shown in Table
4.2-1.
