4.2.2 Overview of economic development
     Guiyang is the capital of Guizhou Province, the province's economic center. 2023, the
city's GDP once again crossed the milestone of a hundred billion, reaching 515.475 billion
yuan, with a year-on-year increase of 6%, the growth rate is higher than that of the country or
the province, its economic operation in general presents a good trend of recovery to good
condition and improved quality during the progress. Among them, the added value of the
primary industry was 20.748 billion yuan, with an increase of 4.0%; the secondary industry,
185.528 billion yuan, with an increase of 5.8%; the tertiary industry 314.200 billion yuan, with
an increase of 6.2%. Per capita GDP was 81,670 yuan, with an increase of 3.4%. The GDP
growth of Gui'an New Area had a year-on-year increase of 24.1%, the growth rate ranked first
in the state-level new areas, a number of economic indicators grew with high-speed, achieved a
good start of "three years of great change", and became a new strong growth point in Guizhou.
The total economic output of Guiyang Gui’an reached 527.804 billion yuan, with an increase




                                                         50
of 6.2% year-on-year, the digital economy accounting for more than 50%, the green economy
accounting for 49%, and the top position further improved to 25.2%.

4.3 Status of the Ecological Environment in Guiyang City
     As a bright green pearl of the Yunnan-Guizhou Plateau, Guizhou is a national ecological
civilization pilot area, with beautiful mountains and rivers, pleasant climate, and peculiar karst
landscape, is an important ecological security barrier in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River
and the Pearl River. "Green" Guiyang is a city established on ecology, as the city's forest
coverage rate reaches 55%, the city has a total of 1025 large, medium, small, and micro-sized
parks, and the per capita area of green park space is more than 14.85 square meters. The city is
extremely rich in wild plant resources. There are 3755 species of vascular plants and 3009
species of seed plants. Guiyang City is rich in wild plant and animal resources (see Section 4.4
in this report for details).

     In terms of water resources, Guiyang City is rich in precipitation, with 1084.0 mm of
precipitation in 2023, but it is difficult to develop and utilize it, and the problem of
engineering-type water shortage is prominent. The total water resources of Guiyang City are
3.136 billion m³ in 2023, which is 23.8% less than the multi-year average of total water
resources, which is 4.117. The total water consumption is 1.001 billion m³, accounting for
24.5% of the multi-year average total water resources, the water resources development and
utilization rate of Guiyang City's various administrative districts varies greatly, with the 6
major districts having a high development and utilization rate, and the water resources of the
three northern counties having a development and utilization rate in the range of 10%~ 25%.

4.4 Status of Biodiversity in the Project Site
     In 2023, the relevant team carried out site survey on Lake Aha National Wetland Park,
and prepared the Background Survey of Biodiversity in Lake Aha National Wetland Park, the
PMO engaged Guiyang City Transportation Planning Survey Design Institute Co., Ltd in April
2025 to prepare the DEIA form for the project, including the special ecological assessment, and
the approval from Guiyang Municipal EEB was obtained on June 4th 2025 (ZHUHUANBIAO
[2025] No.87).

     In conjunction with the Background Survey of Biodiversity in Lake Aha National
Wetland Park and the Special Ecological Assessment Report, this report carried out a
comprehensive assessment of the current status of species diversity in the wetland of Lake Aha
from the perspectives of vegetation diversity, animal diversity and microbial diversity.


                                                 51
4.4.1 Animal diversity
        In terms of animal diversity, the wetland park is inhabited by a large number of wild
animals, including birds, fish and amphibians. Specifically, the animals in Lake Aha Wetland
Park include 34 species of beasts in 8 orders and 16 families; 227 species of birds in 18 orders
and 57 families; 16 species of reptiles in 2 orders and 7 families; 13 species of amphibians in 1
order and 7 families, 10 genera; 24 species of fish in 5 orders and 10 families, 22 genera; 127
species of insects in 11 orders and 71 families; 55 species of arachnids in 16 families, 43
genera; 15 species of zooplankton in 4 categories; 17 species of cave animals in 3 orders and 6
classes, 8 orders, 14 families and 17 genera3.

         (i) Fish

        In the wetland park, there are 24 species of fishes in 5 orders, 10 families and 22 genera,
dominated by taxa distributed in the south and lacking typical northern species. The wide water
surface and deep-water level of Aha Reservoir in the Wetland Park provide a good living
environment for fishes in slow-flowing or still-water environments, especially for Rhodeus
ocellatus, Pseudorasbora parva, Abbottina rivularis, and sharpbelly (Hemiculter leucisculus)
and other small fish which are abundant and are dominant species in Aha Reservoir. Based on
the field survey and site visit, it was determined that the main economic and important fish
species in Lake Aha National Wetland Park are yellow catfish (Tachysurus fulvidraco), crucian
carp (Carassius auratus), carp (Cyprinus carpio), grass carp (Ctenopharyngodon idellus),
bighead carp (Hypophthalmichthys nobilis), silver carp (Hypophthalmichthys molitrix), and
sharpbelly (Hemiculter leucisculus), among which bighead, silver carp, crucian carp, and carp
are more abundant.

        There are more algae and less fish in Baiyan River, Youyu River, Jinzhong River,
Caichong Gully, Lanni Gully and Xiaoche River and other tributaries, with alien invasive
species found through interview and investigation, including 10 species of fish, of which 6
species were found through interview, and only the living Chinese hooksnout carp was
witnessed.

        It is clear from the above information that the project area does not involve rare and
endangered protected fish species.

        (ii) Amphibians and reptiles


3   the Background Survey of Biodiversity in Lake Aha National Wetland Park (2023)




                                                              52
     In the wetland park, there are 13 species of amphibians of 1 order, 7 families, 10 genera;
16 species of reptiles of 2 orders, 7 families. Specifically, there are 8 endemic species in China,
namely Hyla annectans, Rana hanluica, Rana zhenhaiensis, Odorrana kweichowensis,
Takydromus septentrionalis, Takydromus intermedius, Pareas boulengeri, and Amphiesma
craspedogaster. 3 species are in the endangered (EN) level in China Biodiversity Red List -
Vertebrate Volume, namely Pelodiscus sinensis, Elaphe carinata, and Elaphe taeniura; 4
species in the vulnerable (VU) level, namely Oreolalax rhodostigmatus, Quasipaa boulengeri,
Ptyas dhumnades, and Azemiops feae; 2 species in the near-threatened (NT) level, namely
Pelophylax nigromaculatus and Takydromus intermedius.

     (iii) Birds

     There are 227 species of birds of 18 orders and 57 families in the wetland park. According
to the zoogeographical zoning of China, Lake Aha Wetland belongs to the subregion of
Oriental realm - Central China - Western Mountainous Plateau. Among them, there are 3
species of national first-class key protected birds and 32 species of national second-class
key protected birds. According to the National Forestry and Grassland Administration
Announcement No. 23 of 2023, Lake Aha National Wetland Park is classified as one of the
first batch of important habitats for terrestrial wildlife, and the protected species involve
colorful ibis, red-bellied woodpecker, chestnut ducks, and water pheasants. According to the
research data, the birds near Lake Aha are mainly distributed in Kailong Village facing the
mountain in the northwestern part of the park and the areas close to the water of the three rivers
and Xiaoche River in the south. The siting and routing of the project avoided this area to
reduce the disturbance of the project construction to the life of birds, and to improve the quality
of their habitat protection.

     During the survey, the ecological diversity team recorded a total of 39 bird species in
2024. Among them, the common buzzard and the white-bellied harrier are national
second-class protected birds; there are 15 species of waterbirds, all of which are in small
numbers; forest birds are all quite common.

     The project area is relatively rich in bird resources, and the assessment has targeted bird
protection measures.

      (iv) Beasts

     There are 34 species of beasts in 8 orders and 16 families in the wetland park. Due to the
impact of habitat fragmentation on the habitats of the beasts, large beasts and carnivores are


                                                 53
rare, and the rodent species among small beasts are the most numerous and are the dominant
group in the area.

     According to the survey, there are two species of national first-class protected beasts
(forest musk, rasse) and two species of national second-class protected beasts (macaque
monkey, leopard cat) in Lake Aha National Wetland Park.

     During the 2024 field survey by the biodiversity team, only cattle was recorded in the area
of Caichong Gully and Lanni Gully, and no other beasts were recorded.

     (v) Insects

     There are 127 species of insects of 11 orders and 71 families in Lake Aha Wetland Park,
and 3 species of national protected "three kinds of insects". Among them, the dominant family
is Papilionidae, and the dominant species are Pyrrhalta huneralis and Leptocorisa chinensis.
The species richness (D) of Lake Aha Wetland Park was 24.32, the Shannon-Weiener diversity
index (H) was 6.32, and the community evenness was (J) 1.27. Classified from the
characteristics of biological habits of insects, the wetland park had the following four taxa of
insects: phytophagous, predatory, parasitic, and others, with dominance indices of 0.79, 0.11,
0.01 and 0.09 respectively, which concluded that the dominance of phytophagous taxa was the
largest and that of parasitic taxa was the smallest in the area. The dominant individuals in the
phytophagous taxa were Pyrrhalta huneralis and Leptocorisa chinensis, and the dominant
individual in the predatory taxa was Machimus sp.

     Only Pieris rapae, Junonia orithya, and Lampides boeticus were recorded at Wushan
Village, Baiyan River, during the 2024 field survey by the biodiversity team, and no protected
insects were involved.

4.4.2 Plants
     (i) Plant diversity

     Lake Aha Wetland Park has high plant diversity, there are 122 families, 381 genera and
556 species of seed plants, including 543 species of angiosperms (115 families, 370 genera)
and 13 species of gymnosperms (7 families, 11 genera); there are 3 species of national
second-class protected wild plants, which are Emmenopterys henryi Oliv., Machilus
nanmu and Chinese gooseberry. There are 18 families, 38 genera and 59 species of ferns,
including 17 families, 37 genera and 56 species of ferns, 1 family, 1 genus and 3 species of
stone pines; there are 41 families, 76 genera and 147 species of bryophytes; there is one newly



                                                54
recorded species in Guizhou Province. There are 135 species of phytoplankton in 7 families
and 61 genera.

        214 species of plants were recorded in the 2024 field survey; among them, one national
second-class protected plant in the wild state - golden buckwheat (Fagopyrum dibotrys);
one endemic species with a wild state - Camptotheca acuminata; 22 species of exotic plants, of
which 8 are invasive plants, respectively, Pontederia crassipes, Bidens pilosa, Ageratum
conyzoides, Erigeron canadensis, Erigeron annuus, Ipomoea purpurea, Symphyotrichum
subulatum, and Alternanthera philoxeroides.

        (ii) Aquatic plant communities

        There are 124 species of wetland plants in 48 families and 90 genera distributed in the
Wetland Park, with four life types: submerged, floating leaf, floating and emergent, among
which the submerged and emergent types are the majority distributed. Among them,
Alternanthera philoxeroides has two life types, namely, emergent and floating, which is more
distributed in the wetland park and has a larger biomass. The proportion of submerged plants is
also higher, among which Vallisneria natans (Lour.) H. Hara has a larger biomass and is more
typical in wetland parks.

        The aquatic plant community in Lake Aha National Wetland Park mainly consists of three
major types: submerged plants, floating plants and emergent plants. The submerged plant
community is the main aquatic vegetation in Lake Aha Wetland Park, which is characterized
by the plant body being completely submerged in the water, and there are five main
communities: Comm. Vallisneria asiatica, Comm. Hyderilla vertillata, Comm. Potamogeton
malainus, Comm. Potamogeton pectinatus, and Comm. Myriopyllum verticillatum. Floating
water plant community mainly includes Comm. Alternanthera philoxeroides. The emergent
plant community mainly consists of Comm. Phragmites communis.

        Through the field survey of the biodiversity team4, the aquatic plant communities in the
Lake Aha area are of poor quality, with low coverage of submerged plants, and a large variety
of exotic and even invasive species distributed among the hygrophyte, emergent and floating
plants. A total of five species of submerged plants were recorded, with a narrow distribution
range and a small distribution area. The distribution range of submerged plants in Baiyan River
is larger, ranging from Comm. Vallisneria asiatica in the upper reaches to Comm. Myriopyllum


4   Research Report on Lake Aha from Beijing Jinglang Ecological Science and Technology Co.




                                                              55
verticillatum at the lake inlet. The submerged plant wetland in the backwater area of Caichong
Gully is planted with a large area of waterweed, which grows extremely luxuriantly, and this
area is also the water where apple snails are concentrated. There are many species of emergent
plants and hygrophyte plants, totaling 17 species, including the invasive alien species -
Alternanthera philoxeroides and 4 other alien plants. There are 3 species of floating plants in
total, including 1 exotic invasive species, Eichhornia crassipes.

     (iii) Invasive species

     According to the biodiversity survey in 2024, 22 exotic plant species were recorded, of
which 8 are invasive, namely Pontederia crassipes, Bidens pilosa, Ageratum conyzoides,
Erigeron canadensis, Erigeron annuus, Ipomoea purpurea, Symphyotrichum subulatum, and
Alternanthera philoxeroides.

4.4.3 Key protected wildlife
     Combining the two surveys, there are four species of national second-class protected
plants, namely Emmenopterys henryi, Semiliquidambar cathayensis, Actinidia chinensis, and
Fagopyrum dibotrys. The field survey in 2024 recorded Fagopyrum dibotrys in the Jinzhong
River basin, and this project will not affect it as it is only a wetland restoration project at the
inlet of Jinzhong River into the lake.

     There are 38 species of national first-class and second-class protected wild animals in the
      Wetland Park, mainly including Plegadis falcinellus, Chrysolophus pictus, Cygnus
   columbianus, Aix galericulata, Pernis ptilorhynchus, Aviceda leuphotes, Accipiter nisus,
 Dendrocygna javanica, Circus cyaneus, Milvus migrans, Butastur indicus, Buteo japonicus,
  Otus lettia, Glaucidium cuculoides, Falco tinnunculus, Falco subbuteo, Falco peregrinus,
              Moschus berezovskii, Viverricula indica, and Macaca mulatta, etc.

4.4.4 Important habitats
     (i) Bird habitats

     According to the project planning information, there are 2 main areas of bird habitat in
Lake Aha Wetland Park: the Kailong Village area in the northwestern part of the park facing
the mountains, and the branch area of the reservoir in the southern part of the park.

     The northwestern part of the park is covered with lush forests, far away from human
activity areas, with less human interference, which is the best area for birds to roost, and the
status quo of the Kailong Village area is that many birds are found roosting and gathering. The


                                                  56
southern part of the park is the backwater area of Aha Reservoir and the area of Xiaoche River,
because of the low water level of the lake in the fall and winter, a large area of beach is formed,
and because of the surrounding farmland, it attracts a large number and species of waterfowl
groups to forage, roost, breed and live through the winter.

     (ii) Other important habitats

     According to the relevant information and site survey, there is no large-scale or
centralized spawning, feeding, or overwintering site of key protected fish within the assessed
area, and the range of fish activities is quite scattered, with no fixed migratory passage.

4.4.5 Protection status
      (i) Plant diversity conservation program

     In the process of protecting plant diversity, Lake Aha National Wetland Park has taken a
series of effective measures to maintain the integrity and stability of the wetland ecosystem.
The first is to protect the native vegetation in the park and reduce human disturbance. The
park management strictly limits the activities of tourists to avoid direct damage to the
vegetation. At the same time, the park also implements a strict ecological protection system,
strengthens the daily management and maintenance of the vegetation, and ensures that the
natural renewal and succession process of the vegetation is not disturbed. The park has also
strengthened the protection of rare plants and established a detailed plant list and monitoring
system to understand and grasp the growth of plants in a timely manner, providing strong
support for scientific protection. In terms of afforestation and greening, Lake Aha National
Wetland Park has carried out large-scale afforestation and greening work in suitable locations.
The park has selected suitable tree species and vegetation types according to the climate and
soil conditions of the wetland and improved the green coverage of the park through scientific
planting and management. These trees and vegetation not only provide a good ecological
environment for the wetland but also become an important part of the wetland ecosystem,
providing habitats and breeding places for organisms in the wetland.

     Lake Aha National Wetland Park has also invested a great deal of energy and resources in
the restoration and reconstruction of vegetation in damaged habitats in the park. Through the
restoration and reconstruction of vegetation, the park has effectively improved the ecological
environment of the wetland and enhanced the self-regulation and stability of the ecosystem. At
the same time, the park also focuses on the scientific and sustainable nature of vegetation
restoration and reconstruction to ensure that the restored and reconstructed vegetation can be


                                                  57
truly integrated into the wetland ecosystem and contribute to the long-term development of the
wetland.

     Through the implementation of these measures, the plant diversity of Lake Aha National
Wetland Park has been effectively protected, and the wetland ecosystem has shown good
development. The park has a rich variety of vegetation and a stable ecological structure,
providing a good habitat and breeding environment for organisms in the wetland. At the same
time, the park also actively carries out science popularization and education activities to raise
public awareness of plant diversity and its protection, which lays a solid social foundation for
the protection of plant diversity.

     (ii) Animal Diversity Conservation Program

     In Lake Aha National Wetland Park, thanks to strong ecological protection measures, rare
species such as the green-headed duck, a bird under national first-class protection, and the
white pheasant, a wild animal under national second-class key protection, have been found in
the park, and the discovery of these species not only set a new record for the number of animal
and plant species in the park, but also reflected the effectiveness of the protection work.

     Apart from direct conservation measures, publicity and education are equally important.
Strengthening publicity and education on animal protection can enhance public awareness of
animal diversity and conservation. The public is an important force in animal protection.
Through publicity and education, more people can be made aware of the value and ecological
functions of wild animals, so that they can consciously participate in animal protection actions.
For example, animal protection lectures, exhibitions and other activities can be organized on a
regular basis to enable the public to understand the ecological habits and conservation
knowledge of wild animals and enhance their conservation awareness. Meanwhile, animal
protection courses can also be strengthened in school education to cultivate children's
awareness of animal protection from an early age.

     In addition, the prevention, control and monitoring of animal diseases is also an important
part of wildlife protection. Wild animals may carry various viruses and parasites, which pose a
threat to humans and other animals. Therefore, the Park Management Office should strengthen
the prevention, control and monitoring of animal diseases to detect and deal with animal
epidemics in a timely manner to ensure the health and safety of wild animals. This includes
strengthening the monitoring and early warning of wildlife epidemics, enhancing the
development and use of vaccines, and improving the capacity of animal epidemic prevention.


                                                  58
Through these measures, the risk of occurrence and spread of wildlife epidemics can be
effectively reduced to protect the health of wildlife and the safety of human beings5 .

4.4.6 Threatening factors
        (i) Higher levels of disturbance to terrestrial vegetation in the Lake Aha basin

        Drylands are widely distributed in the flat valleys and gently sloping areas of the Lake
Aha basin. High forests are mainly found in areas with large slopes that are not suitable for
cultivation as farmland, and the distribution of broadleaf evergreen forests is narrow, with only
small patches on steep slopes at the mouth of the Baiyan River, which is less traveled by
people. There is a large area of farmland located on the top of the hill and on the gentle slopes
of the waterfront that is abandoned. In the basin, due to the impact of town development and
construction and human activities, the topsoil is damaged without timely greening, and some
areas have low vegetation cover and exposed rock and soil, resulting in soil erosion. To address
this problem, this feasibility study carries out forest vegetation restoration works on the north
side of Lake Aha.

        (ii) Poor state of the aquatic ecosystems in the Lake Aha basin

        The Lake Aha basin has low coverage of submerged plant communities and a high variety
of exotic and even invasive species in hydrophyte, emergent and floating plants. The species
and quantity of fish are low. Snail populations are unevenly distributed and have a high
mortality rate. Crustaceans such as shrimp were not seen. Apple snail, an exotic invasive
species, is widely distributed. There is an urgent need to restore healthy water ecosystems in
the Lake Aha basin to enhance the self-purification of the water body by restoring the diversity
of aquatic communities. To address this issue, this project will carry out a river water
ecological restoration project in the Lake Aha basin, remove invasive species, release fish and
benthic organisms, and plant submerged and emergent plants to improve the ecological
environment.

        (iii) Low bird species and numbers in the Lake Aha basin

        Birds with high numbers in the Lake Aha basin are all widespread and common species,
such as egrets, little grebes, yellow-rumped bulbuls, and so on. The distribution of waterbirds is
closely related to the type of habitat they require, e.g., brown river crow, white-topped brook
robin, and red-tailed water robin are distributed in the channels of various tributaries, and gulls

5   Master Plan of Lake Aha National Wetland Park, Guiyang, Guizhou, China




                                                             59
are distributed in the waters of the big lake area of Lake Aha, but all are in small, single-digit
numbers. This is because of the high degree of disturbance to terrestrial vegetation and the poor
ecosystem structure of water bodies.

     (iv) Higher levels of human disturbances such as angling and cages in the Lake Aha
basin

     The waterfront of the Lake Aha basin is heavily populated by anglers, and multiple
ground cages were found in the backwater area of Caichong Gully, thus killing large numbers
of benthic animals such as snails, river clams, and Semisulcospira snail. Human disturbance
has caused persistent negative interference with the stability of the wetland aquatic community.

     (v) Introduction of invasive alien species by inappropriate wetland restoration
actions

     Existing artificial wetlands used for water purification in the Lake Aha area is mainly
planted with exotic plants, such as waterweed, Pontederia cordata, Canna indica, and Thalia
dealbata, etc. The eggs and young snails of apple snails will be introduced into the lake area
along with these exotic plants, which will lead to the widespread distribution of apple snails.
To address this problem, the project needs to take measures to control the population size of
existing invasive species and to clean up the project area of exotic species, such as upgrading
the wetland at the inlet of Jinzhong River, and the gradual replacement of exotic species such
as waterweed, Pontederia cordata, Canna indica, and Thalia dealbata by native plants in the
existing wetland. In the subsequent restoration of the wetland ecosystem, native plants and
animals should be used to avoid the introduction of invasive alien species to the greatest extent
possible.

     (vi) More serious point source and surface source pollution in the Lake Aha basin

     According to the project feasibility study information, the wastewater treatment rate in
Lake Aha is about 50%, and the centralized treatment rate is 30%. Although there are urban
municipal pipeline network and urban wastewater treatment plants and other facilities in the
towns around the basin, the pipeline network coverage is incomplete, old, and broken with
problems of "overflowing, bubbling, dripping, and leaking", which leads to wastewater mixed
with rainwater and ultimately discharged into the river. And for the rural areas in the basin, the
wastewater treatment facilities are not perfect, there are also quite a lot of wastewater directly
or indirectly discharged into the river, bringing impacts on the tributaries and even on the water
quality of the Aha Reservoir. In response to this problem, the project carries out the


                                                 60
construction of Lake Aha interceptor pipeline network, which collects and transports the
regional domestic wastewater to the existing Erqiao Wastewater Treatment Plant and Xiaohe
Wastewater Treatment Plant for treatment. The domestic wastewater along Baiyan River and
Youyu River is collected and used for agricultural irrigation after being treated to the standard
by the wastewater treatment station.

monitoring information of two lakes and one reservoir combined with on-site monitoring, the
water quality of the project area is shown in the following table.

4.5.2 Status of bottom sludge quality
          This EIA set up a bottom sludge monitoring at about 200m upstream of the lake inlet of
Lanni Gully. The bottom sludge monitoring was carried out by Guizhou Duansheng
Environmental Protection Technology Co., Ltd on January 10th 2025, with one time of
monitoring, and the monitoring factors include 11 indicators, namely pH, Hg, Cd, Cr, Cr6+, As,
Pb, Ni, benzo(a)pyrene, Be, Ag.

        It can be seen through the monitoring results8 of bottom sludge that the bottom sludge
basically meets the standard requirements of the soil pollution screening value for agricultural
land in the Soil Environmental Quality Standards for Soil Pollution Risk Control Standards for
Agricultural Land (Trial).

4.5.3 Status of atmospheric quality
        The status quo analysis of air environment quality in this EIA cites relevant data from the
"Guiyang City 2023 Ecological Environment Status Bulletin": In 2023, Guiyang City had 363
days of good ambient air quality, of which 230 days were Class I (excellent), 133 days were
Class II (good), and 2 days were Class III (mildly polluted), with the proportion of days with
good ambient air quality at 99.5%, and the monitoring results of each basic pollutant all meet
the standards. The air environment quality in the project area is good.

4.5.4 Status of sound quality
        According to the project status and the surrounding acoustic environment sensitive points,

4.6 Status of Aha Reservoir Dam Safety
         Aha Reservoir is a medium-sized reservoir located on Xiaoche River, a tributary of
Nanming River in Guiyang City, belonging to Wujiang River system. The controlled rainfall
collection area upstream the dam is 190 square kilometers, which is 8 kilometers away from
the city center. Aha Reservoir was designed in April 1958, the construction started in August
of the same year the first phase of construction was completed in June 1960, and the project
was completed in 1965. The main functions of the reservoir in the early stage were flood
control, fish farming, agriculture and irrigation, and it was designated as a source of drinking
water in 1982. The drinking water function has been cancelled in 2023, and the main function
is flood control and ecological water use now.

         The key structure of Aha Lake reservoir project is mainly composed of dam, spillway,
layered water intake and drainage tunnel and dam bottom culvert. The dam is a clay inclined
wall dam with a crest elevation of 1115.0m, a maximum dam height of 38.0m, a crest width of
36.0m and a crest length of 133.0 m. According to the Preliminary Report on the Emergency
Reinforcement Project of Aha Lake Reservoir in Guiyang City10, the design flood standard is
once in 100 years (P=1%), the response peak flood discharge of 706m³/s, and the design flood
level of 1112.50m; The check flood standard is once in 2000 (P=0.05%), the response to the
peak inflow flood flow of 1170 m³/s, the check flood level of 1113.62m. The normal storage
water level of the reservoir is 1110.0m, the dead water level is 1096.5m, the utilizable storage
capacity is 39.412 million m³, and the dead storage capacity is 9.798 million m³.




9    Environmental Status Quo Monitoring for Guiyang Green Urban Development Project (Report No.: DH2501072)
10   Prepared by Kunming Survey and Design Institute Co., Ltd of China Power Group in October 2017




                                                              63
        The Aha Reservoir Dam was certified as a Category 311 dam in 2017 and has since been
reinforced. The PMO engaged independent dam safety experts to carry out site survey and
assessment in February 2025. According to the assessment results12, Aha Reservoir Dam
belongs to Category 1 dam, that is, the dam flood resistance standard meets the flood
control standard, and the reservoir dam works normally; the reservoir dam has no major
quality problems and is in normal operation according to design standards.

4.7 Red Line for Ecological Protection in the Project Area
        The area of the red line of ecological protection within the basin of the Aha Reservoir is
1,410.06 hectares. The red line of ecological protection is mainly concentrated in Lake Aha
National Wetland Park with an area of 1,047.58 hectares and the International Ecotourism
Resort with an area of 221.91 hectares.

        Lake Aha National Wetland Park belongs to the provincial important wetland and national
nature park, according to the Wetland Protection Law and the Measures for the Management of
National Nature Parks, the boundary of Lake Aha National Wetland Park is within the general
control area of the nature reserve system, and the entire park is also within the red line of
ecological protection.

        According to the Announcement of the State Forestry and Grassland Administration (No.
23 of 2023) (List of Important Habitats for Terrestrial Wildlife (the first batch)), Lake Aha
National Wetland Park in Guiyang, Guizhou, was designated by the State Forestry and
Grassland Administration in January 2024 as one of the first 789 important habitats for wildlife,
with the same geographic coordinates as Lake Aha National Wetland Park.

        In conclusion: Lake Aha National Wetland Park overlaps with the scope of important
habitats and is a general control area in the nature reserve system, both of which are located in
Guiyang City within the ecological protection red line.

4.8 Physical Cultural Resources
        According to the survey conducted by Guiyang Municipal Bureau of Culture and Tourism,
there are 29 immovable cultural relics in the planning area of Lake Aha, among which there is
one county-level cultural relics protection site, i.e. the Li's Residence in Baishao Village,
Shiban Town, Huaxi District. After investigation, the construction of the project will not affect
these cultural relics13 .

4.9 Current Status of Forestry Pests and Diseases in Guiyang
        Principles of prevention and control of pests and diseases in Guiyang: fully
implement the policies and responsibilities of prevention and control of forestry pests and
diseases with “prevention as priority, scientific treatment, lawful supervision, and strengthened
responsibilities”, and follow the principles of taking categorized measures and seeking both


13   Social Impact Assessment Report




                                                65
temporary and permanent solutions for different situations, and combining the technical
measures for forest culture and management, biological measures and chemical prevention and
control. Based on the technical measures for forest culture and management, put great efforts in
green prevention and control, such as biological prevention and control and prevention and
control with bionic preparation, reduce and rationalize chemical pesticides, guarantee the
effects of prevention and control, strictly prevent hazardous forestry pests, such as pine wilt
disease, from appearing, transmitting, or spreading in Gui’an, Guiyang, and protect the safety
of forest resources and ecological environment in Gui’an, Guiyang.

     Institutional arrangement: the prevention and control of forestry pests in 2024 was
organized, guided, inspected, and reviewed by Guiyang Municipal Forestry Bureau. The pest
prevention and control stations of the Bureau guided and managed the forestry pest prevention
and control work throughout the entire city, including the preparation of prevention and control
plan, the organization of expert review on the implementation plan of prevention and control
by each unit, the inspection and supervision on the progress and effects of prevention and
control, the coordination and handling of issues in the prevention and control work, and the
summary and report after the prevention and control work is completed. The relevant
departments of each district (municipality/county) or bureau is responsible for preparing the
implementation plan for prevention and control and organizing the prevention and control
work.

     Prevention and control measures: (i) strengthen monitoring and early warning and
implement full-area monitoring. Conduct monitoring and early warning by taking site survey,
remote survey, and trap survey, with the full-time and part-time monitoring and reporting
personnel of the monitoring and reporting network system on the municipal, county, and
township levels and the staff of the forestry stations carefully conducting year-long monitoring
and fixed monitoring to accurately grasp the appearance and development trend of forestry
pests and timely publishing the trend forecast and warning information (there are two
pandemic monitoring spots in Lake Aha for patrol and monitoring throughout the year). (ii)
strengthen quarantine management and strictly implement quarantine supervision and law
enforcement. Conduct quarantine on the place of origin of seedlings in spring and autumn
(there is one seedling production unit in Lake Aha Wetland, with a nursery area of 2 hectares).
(iii) take practical, effective, and rational comprehensive technologies and measures for
prevention and control, which are specific to the biological properties, biological habits, and
characteristics of hazards of different kinds of pests, such as clearing the withered pine trees,



                                                66
installing traps for longicorns; take measures such as spraying powder for Beauveria bassiana
or artificial catching and killing to prevent Hylobitelus, Dendrolimus, and Phasmida, etc.

     Current status of prevention and control: according to the Implementation Status of
Forestry Pests Prevention and Control Stations of Guiyang City in the Fourth Quarter of 2024,
Guiyang City has completed the autumn survey on pine wilt disease. 1.9149 million mu of pine
forest was surveyed in autumn, and 2482 samples were collected, and 2482 samples were
examined by microscopy, with a microscopy rate of 100%. According to the survey, there was
no pine wilt disease found throughout the city. The quarantine and investigation on the place of
origin of seedlings in autumn and daily monitoring and prevention and control work were
completed. The disaster rate of forestry pests in 2024 was 0, the pollution-free prevention and
control rate reached 99.9%, the accuracy of forecast reached 98%, the quarantine rate of the
place of origin of forest seedlings reached 100%, and the objectives of forestry pests
prevention and control were achieved.




                                                67
5 Alternative Comparison

     The analysis of alternatives is intended to optimize the project design from the
environmental aspect, to compare and analyze the scope and degree of impact of the different
design alternatives of the project on the ecological environment, and to recommend the
optimization of the design of the project from the perspective of environmental protection, and
to provide a scientific basis for decision-making for the construction of the project. The general
principles of alternative comparison and analysis:

        Quantitative   comparison    principle:     The   environmental   impacts    of   project
         implementation are quantified as much as possible for each alternative.

        Comprehensive comparison principle: Comprehensive comparative analysis from the
         environment, technology, economy and other aspects.

5.1 Comparison between Implementing and Not Implementing the Project
     The EIA has analyzed the pros and cons between implementing and not implementing the
project (see Preliminary Environmental Impact Assessment). The analysis shows that the
project implementation will expand the forest area and improve the habitat quality, which will
enhance the wildlife population, biodiversity and ecosystem service function, and enhance the
carbon sink, which will have significant environmental benefits, and at the same time facilitate
the sustainable development of the community. The project will generate some negative
environmental impacts, which can be eliminated or reduced to a small level after taking
environmental impact mitigation measures. The environmental and social benefits of the
project are much greater than the negative environmental impacts that can be avoided by not
implementing the project.

     In conclusion, the implementation of the project is very necessary.

5.2 Alternatives Analysis
     The EIA has conducted alternative comparison for 8 sections of the greenway namely
main route of greenway in east Aha Village section (K0+300~K0+700), main route of
greenway in Caeryan Bridge section, main route of greenway in northwest section with dense
forest land, natural sand and stone forest trail, elevated trail along the mountain, wetland
greenway, field greenway, and suburban greenway (see Preliminary Environmental Impact
Assessment). The preferred route was determined in conjunction with the controlling factors




                                                   68
along the route, as well as topography, ecology, landscape, and land acquisition and
resettlement.

     The preferred alternatives are in line with the national and local laws and regulations,
meet the requirements of industrial technical specifications, construction quality, and passage
safety, while the occupation of forest land and lake surface is reduced, causing smaller impacts
on the ecological environment.
