                                                 71
6.1 Analysis on the Impacts of Category 2 Technical Assistance
     Category 2 mainly includes policy study (accounting of carbon emission reduction of
green account, study on conversion and incentive mechanism, methodological study on karst
carbon sink), and preparation of planning (low carbon urban planning of Guiyang City).

     The purpose for preparing the relevant policy study and planning is to promote the
scientific and reasonable survey, monitoring, and protection of biodiversity, and this kind of
activity itself has no direct impact on the environment, but its later implementation may
involve field monitoring, sampling and analysis, which may have potential environmental risks
and impacts. The analysis on these impacts is shown in Chapter 8 and 9.

     Therefore, the corresponding TOR should be prepared for the Category 2 technical
assistance. Such TOR should incorporate the ESF policies, identify the ES risks, and
propose the requirements on staff input/outcomes, and the requirements on stakeholder
engagement. Stakeholder engagement should be conducted during the technical assistance, in
the meantime, the environmental risks and impacts in the later implementation stage
should be considered in the study or the result documents prepared, and the mitigation
measures should be proposed in accordance with the Bank’s Environmental and Social
Standards (ESS).

6.2 Analysis on the Impacts of Category 3 Technical Assistance
     Category 3 mainly includes various biodiversity monitoring, survey, scientific research,
training, propaganda and education, effectiveness evaluation, and establishment of
management institutions etc. The environmental impacts of this kind of technical assistance
mainly lie in the implementation process of the specific activity, such as the monitoring, survey,
and propaganda and education activities conducted in the ecologically sensitive areas, which
may cause negative impacts on the ecological environment. In addition, this kind of technical
assistance itself may involve civil works, such as the nature education path and the
popularization, propaganda, and commentary activities within Lake Aha National Wetland Park
based on the monitoring and study results of biodiversity, which require the construction of
various nature education and commentary facilities, hence the potential negative environmental
impacts. The environmental impacts of Category 3 are similar to those of visitor sightseeing
and maintenance activities, and the relevant analysis has been incorporated in Chapter 9.




                                                 72
7 Analysis on the Environmental Risks and Impacts during the Design
   Period

7.1 Ecological and Environmental Protection
     To mitigate the impacts of the project construction on the ecological environment, many
program adjustments have been carried out during the project design process to reduce the
project's occupation of forest land and ecological protection red line. Meanwhile, the PMO has
engaged Guiyang City Transportation Planning Survey Design Institute Co., Ltd to conduct
more detailed Domestic Environmental Impact Assessment (DEIA), including special
ecological assessment.

     The ecological environmental impact analysis and protection measures are shown in
Chapter 10 of this report and in the Special Ecological Assessment Report.

7.2 Environmental Pollution Prevention and Control Design
    (1) Impact analysis
     The construction and operation process of civil works, as well as the lives of construction
workers of various works will generate wastewater, exhaust gas, solid waste and other
pollutants, which, if discharged directly into the environment, can cause environmental
pollution to the atmosphere, water bodies and soil. Noise will be generated during construction
or operation of some project activities, which will affect the surrounding communities. The
above environmental pollution impacts can be avoided or mitigated by adopting corresponding
prevention and control measures; pollution prevention and control measures should be
incorporated in the project design phase into the design. The project design includes
environmental sanitation facilities, oil smoke purification devices, sludge storage facilities, etc.,
to ensure that the wastewater, exhaust gas, and domestic garbage generated during the
operation period of the project will be properly treated.

    (2) Mitigation measures
     Construction design:

        The construction site is arranged as far away as possible from protected targets such as
residences, schools, hospitals, and natural parks;

        The construction arrangement should make full use of the permanently occupied area
of the project, avoiding and reducing temporary roads or temporary construction sites
established outside the occupied area;


                                                  73
        The design of the construction program should pay attention to the balance of earth
and rock to avoid off-site soil extraction and disposal;

        Construction sites and material stockpiling areas of construction sites, temporary
dumps of construction waste, temporary storage facilities for hazardous wastes, etc. should be
arranged far away from surface water bodies, with more than 50m from rivers, ditches,
reservoirs and other water bodies;

        Construction camps, construction sites, construction waste dumps, and temporary
storage facilities for hazardous waste shall not be located within the boundaries of rivers,
canals, or reservoir dikes;

        Incorporate construction waste reduction targets and measures and hazardous waste
management requirements into the bidding documents or contracts for design, construction and
supervision.

     Project design:

        Activities generating domestic wastewater during the operation period should
incorporate domestic wastewater collection, treatment and reuse measures into the detailed
project design. Domestic wastewater from bus terminals, public parking, etc should be
discharged into the municipal wastewater network; domestic wastewater from other activities is
treated according to local conditions through integrated domestic wastewater treatment and
reuse facilities, septic tanks and other wastewater treatment facilities, the effluent is reused for
greening, agriculture and forestry watering, etc., and shall not be directly discharged into the
environment;

        Trash cans should be reasonably placed in each field propaganda and education site,
outdoor museum, and other outdoor touring areas;

        Green isolation belts should be designed around the proposed science and public
education facilities and their parking lots when they are adjacent to residential houses and the
park;

        Road pavement uses modified asphalt concrete, and practice shows that the noise
value can be reduced by 3～ 5dB (A) on modified asphalt concrete pavement compared to
ordinary asphalt concrete pavement;




                                                  74
          Regarding rural domestic wastewater, treatment modes and technologies should be
selected according to local conditions, considering the quality and quantity of wastewater as
well as the changing characteristics of wastewater, and the design capacity of treatment
facilities should match the population, and the actual amount of wastewater generated;

          Contractors engaged in the construction of building projects in Guizhou Province
should have a good environmental credit record. When bidding for contractors, the PIU should
include environmental credit records as conditions for bidding.

7.3 Water conservation design
        (1) Impact analysis
        Public parking lots, landscape stations, etc. involve energy and water use on a large scale.
Energy-saving and water-saving design should be considered from the design stage. The
parking lot of this project adopts permeable pavement, and a rainwater collection system is set
up, so that the collected rainwater is used for greening irrigation and road washing.

        The project's wastewater works, sidewalk pavement and landscaping works use sponge
city design concepts to delay the peak of stormwater runoff and remove pollutants such as
phosphorus, nitrogen, and heavy metals from stormwater runoff to a certain extent.

        (2) Mitigation measures
          In the construction of greenways and landscape attractions, the sponge city concept
and LID (Low Impact Development) strategy will be integrated, and this project applies the
sponge city design strategy of "infiltration, stagnation, storage, purification, utilization and
drainage" in the construction of greenways and landscape attractions. It enables the natural
accumulation, infiltration, purification and utilization of rainwater, and at the same time
improves the ecological environment quality and flood prevention and drainage capacity of the
city;

          The project's sponge city works mainly contain stormwater works, wastewater works,
sidewalk pavement, greening works, and related sponge city facilities;

          The project's greenway partially uses natural pavement and installs grass-planting
ditches, etc., so that rainwater can quickly infiltrate into the ground, reducing surface runoff
and replenishing groundwater;




                                                   75
        Depressed green spaces will be built in low-lying areas within the greenway to take
advantage of the terrain to retain rainwater, and at the same time serve as a place for tourists to
relax and get close to nature;

        The design phase of road and parking lot incorporates the concept of sponge city and
makes full use of rainwater resources. For example, rainwater collection wells and cellars are
constructed in conjunction with construction and landscape works, and rainwater is collected
and utilized for landscaping, greening, sweeping, and toilet flushing after appropriate
treatment.

7.4 Energy Efficiency Design
     (1) Impact analysis
     The use of construction machinery during the construction of the project as well as
lighting and monitoring systems during operation involves the utilization of energy. The
following measures are proposed to improve energy efficiency.

     (2) Mitigation measures
        Construction techniques for prefabricated components, such as prefabricated bridges
and walkway slabs, are used, whereby some of the components are manufactured in factories
and then transported to the site for installation. This approach reduces on-site concrete pouring,
curing, and other processes, and reduces the energy demand and carbon emissions of on-site
construction;

        The lighting system of the greenway adopts energy efficient LED lamps and is equipped
with an intelligent control system that automatically adjusts the brightness according to the flow of
people and natural light conditions at different times of the day. At night, when the flow of people is low,
the brightness of the lighting is lowered to achieve energy saving effect. In addition, the lighting system
also adopts complementary solar and wind power supply, with the installation of solar streetlights
and small wind power generators in some sections of the road, to further reduce the dependence on
the traditional power grid;

        The pumping stations and wastewater treatment facilities in the interception trench have
adopted energy-efficient pumps, fans and motors, and have realized the on-demand operation of
equipment through frequency conversion and speed control technology, to avoid using a powerful
engine for a light load. Regular maintenance of the equipment is carried out to ensure that the
equipment is in good operating condition and to improve the efficiency of energy utilization. At
the same time, information technology is used to carry out real-time monitoring and data analysis


                                                      76
of the operation of the interception trench, so that energy waste and abnormal operation can be
detected in a timely manner.

8 Analysis of Environmental Risks and Impacts during Construction

8.1 Analysis of Ecological and Environmental Impacts
     See Chapter 10 of this report, Ecological and Environmental Impacts and Analysis, and
the Special Ecological Assessment Report for details.

8.2 Impact of Environmental Pollution on Water Bodies
8.2.1   Water Quality Impacts and Analysis
    (1) Impact analysis
     The project involves bridges and other water-related projects, greenway construction
activities whose proposed locations are relatively close to surface water bodies, and
construction wastewater and domestic wastewater generated during the construction, if not
effectively collected and treated and directly discharged into neighboring surface water bodies,
can cause water pollution. In addition, some of the components of the construction materials or
construction waste or the materials themselves may enter the water bodies due to rainfall, flash
floods, etc., and cause water quality pollution or river cross-section blockage and other
problems. With the end of construction activities, the above risks will end.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        Construction wastewater:

       Construction wastewater diversion and collection measures are taken in accordance
with local conditions to collect wastewater from muddy water, cleaning of construction
materials, concrete maintenance, and washing of vehicles and machinery. The collected
construction wastewater is precipitated and treated and then reused for vehicle washing,
sprinkling and dust suppression, and is not discharged into water bodies;

       Temporary construction wastewater storage and treatment facilities such as
sedimentation tanks should be impermeable;

       Mud generated during bridge construction is treated and recycled, and waste mud is
treated and transported to designated locations for disposal as required;

       Construction materials and wastes such as gravel and earthwork are gathered for
storage, and covered in a timely manner;



                                                 77
          Stormwater interception and diversion facilities should be established around the
construction site and material storage site;

          The training to construction staff should be strengthened, to raise their environmental
awareness. Dumping of wastewater, garbage, and solid wastes into rivers, ditches, or other
surface water bodies should be prohibited;

          For road reconstruction that parallels with Lake Aha Reservoir and construction
projects adjacent to water bodies, material storage areas on the construction sites are arranged
within the site and away from the surface water body;

          Temporary blocking and water diversion measures should be taken on the side
adjacent to the water body to prevent construction materials from rolling down into the water
body or construction wastewater from entering the water body;

           Oily wastewater:

          Liquid construction materials are stored in closed containers. Hazardous construction
materials such as oils, paints and chemicals should be stored in warehouses; if they are stacked,
they should be covered by sheds and tarpaulins;

          River construction process must ensure that the construction machinery is trouble-free,
to eliminate overflowing, bubbling, dripping, leaking, etc., and the one with malfunction during
the process of use should be immediately driven back to the shore for repair; For the machinery
that cannot be moved, if dripping or leaking is found, it should be immediately collected by
containers and transported back to the shore for the proper treatment;

           Domestic wastewater:

          No construction camp will be established during the construction period of the project,
the construction staff will rent the houses from the residents along the road, the domestic
wastewater from the construction staff during the construction period will be collected through
the septic tanks in the residents’ house and sent to the existing wastewater treatment plant in
Guiyang City through the municipal wastewater pipe network;

          The construction staff on the site will use the resident toilets near the construction
area.

        With the above control measures in place, the risk of surface water pollution from the
project's construction activities can be further minimized.



                                                  78
8.2.2 Impacts on hydrological regime and analysis
     See the project flood justification report for details.

8.3 Impacts of Air Pollution
    (1) Impact analysis
     The civil works will generate dust, vehicle exhaust, machine exhaust, asphalt fumes, and
other pollutants during the construction period, which will have an impact on the air
environment. This impact occurs only during the construction period and ends with the
completion of construction activities.

    (2) Mitigation Measures
     Construction Dust:

        The construction sites should be installed with hard enclosure, and the "six 100%s"
requirements will apply to all construction sites for dust management following local
regulations;

        The exposed ground for operation shall be sprinkled with water on a regular basis; the
exposed ground for without operation for the time being shall be greened, paved or covered.
Construction roads should be hardened with simple gravel road surface, etc., and regularly
sprinkled, cleaned, maintained and kept in good operating condition. Vehicle speed is restricted
within the construction site;

        Earthworks should avoid dry and windy weather as much as possible, and earthwork
should be carried out in a wet manner along the excavation and transit routes. Excavation,
backfilling and other earthwork operations should be supplemented by measures such as
sprinkling and dust suppression, and the frequency of sprinkling and dust reduction should be
increased when it comes to dry and windy weather;

        In accordance with the relevant requirements of the Guizhou Province Heavy
Pollution Weather Emergency Response Plan, after the start of the heavy pollution weather
warning, the construction site should stop earthworks, building demolition, spraying and
painting, slope protection and shotcrete, and concrete mixing.

        Continuous watering or spraying (drenching) to suppress dust during road cutting,
crushing, drilling and other construction work;

        Construction materials and earth stockpiled on site are covered with dustproof cloth to
prevent materials from dispersing and forming dust; spoils, abandoned materials and other


                                                   79
construction waste should be removed and transported in a timely manner, and measures such
as covering and spraying dust suppressant should be taken to reduce the generation of dust
during temporary storage in the site; construction waste shall not be piled up outside the
construction site enclosure;

        Use commercial concrete and avoid on-site mixing; where on-site mixing of
ready-mixed concrete and ready-mixed mortar is required due to special circumstances,
centralized and closed mixing should be adopted, and dust reduction treatment should be
carried out;

        The routing of access roads for civil works should be aligned with the project road as
much as possible, and road pavement should be completed in the early stage of construction;

        The car wash platform is established inside the exit for material, slag, garbage
transport vehicles, and the tires and chassis of the vehicles should be washed on the platform
before leaving the site, without mud brought on the road;

        Transportation vehicles should be driven in accordance with the speed limit;

        The transportation of bulk construction materials, slag and other materials should be
carried out in closed containers; when open-top trucks are used for transportation, the materials
on the trucks should be covered with tarpaulins in an airtight manner. It is recommended that
water sprinkling, and dust reduction measures (twice a day) be taken on the roads passing
through villages to reduce road dust;

        Burning of solid waste is prohibited.

     Vehicle and machinery exhaust:

        Encourage the use of new energy vehicles for transportation, the use of diesel vehicles
for transportation must be above the national Class-V standard vehicles, new purchases of
diesel vehicles must be Class-VI standard vehicles;

        Use highly efficient energy-saving and environmental-friendly construction machinery,
diesel power units and high-quality fuel, and regularly maintain diesel engines, diesel
generators and other equipment;

        Encourage the use of new energy non-road mobile machinery; priority should be given
to the fuel-fired non-road mobile machinery with National Class-IV and above standards, and




                                                 80
the use of non-road mobile machinery with emission standards below National Class-III should
be prohibited.

     Asphalt paving fumes:

       It is recommended that the contractors pay attention to controlling the temperature of
asphalt concrete while meeting the requirements of construction, try to reduce the paving
temperature, take water-cooling measures after pavement, which can significantly reduce the
generated emission;

       Paving machinery should have good sealing and dust removal devices, the maximum
allowable emission concentration and the maximum allowable emission rate should meet the
corresponding requirements of the "Comprehensive Emission Standards for Air Pollutants"
(GB16297- 1996), and there should be no obvious disorganized emissions from the production
equipment;

       For the road sections where environmentally sensitive targets such as residential sites
exist in the vicinity, operation on sunny and windy days with good conditions for atmospheric
diffusion should be selected for asphalt concrete paving.

     With the above control measures in place, the impact on air environment from the
project's construction activities can be further minimized.

8.4 Impacts of Noise Pollution
    (1) Impact analysis
     Noise sources during the construction of civil works activities include noise generated by
various types of construction machinery, such as excavators, bulldozers, air compressors,
cranes, chainsaws, pavers, rollers, piling rigs and other noise generated by the operation of
these machines, as well as noise from large transportation vehicles, such as heavy-duty
transportation trucks, which will have an impact on the normal life and work of people at the
sound environmental protection targets, such as residential areas and schools, around the
construction site. The impact of noise from the activities is short-term, and the impact of
acoustic environment will end when the construction activities are completed.

     Meanwhile, the PMO has engaged Guiyang City Transportation Planning Survey Design
Institute Co., Ltd to carry out more detailed Domestic Environmental Impact Assessment
(DEIA), including special acoustic environmental assessment. The detailed analysis on noise




                                                 81
source strength and impact forecast can be found in the Special Acoustic Environmental
Assessment Report.

    (2) Mitigation Measures
        The main noise prevention and control measures and construction facilities will be
reported to the environmental monitoring department for review and filing;

        The construction sites will be surrounded by hard enclosure, which can effectively
mitigate the spread of noise;

        For the activities located in the town area and surrounding the existence of acoustic
environmental protection targets, the construction time strictly comply with local regulations,
noise-generating construction operations are prohibited at night (22:00 pm ~ 6:00 the next day);
if nighttime construction is really needed due to special circumstances, a nighttime
construction permit should be obtained in accordance with local requirements;

        The contractors should make public announcements about the construction
information of the project before construction, communicate with the neighboring communities
in advance about the construction arrangements, and arrange the noise-generating construction
activities in the time with less impact;

        The contractors must use construction machinery and transportation vehicles that meet
the relevant national standards and take temporary noise mitigation measures. Low-noise
construction machinery and processes should be selected as much as possible, fixed
mechanical equipment with intense vibration should be equipped with vibration-damping seat
(idle equipment should be turned off immediately), fixed strong noise sources should be
covered with soundproof enclosure, and the maintenance of all types of construction equipment,
should be strengthened at the same time to maintain its good operation, in order to reduce the
strength of noise source from the beginning;

        When there are acoustic environment sensitive buildings in the vicinity, the noise at
the site boundary during the construction period shall comply with the Environmental Noise
Emission Standards for Construction Site Boundaries (GB12523-2011);

        For the 8 sensitive points (Jinshan Village, Lijiazhuang, Houba, Xingfu Community,
Xiaba Village, Zhulin Village, Bangbao Village and Xiangjiaqiao) which are close to the project
route and the construction area, the noise will exceed the standard during construction, and it is
proposed to adopt measures such as shortening the construction time when multiple equipment



                                                 82
are working at the same time, constructing mobile sound barriers in relatively concentrated
places of fixed construction equipment and forbidding the construction of noisy equipment at
night at 22:00～ 06:00. Noise mitigation measures will be taken by installing temporary
mobile sound barriers during construction near the above sensitive points;

        Reasonable arrangement of transportation routes and time periods, avoiding
noise-sensitive areas (e.g., villages) and time periods (e.g., nighttime) as much as possible;
arbitrary rerouting is strictly prohibited;

        When vehicles and construction machinery cross villages, travel speeds are limited
(generally no more than 20km/h) and sounding of horns is prohibited. Heavy vehicles should
be fitted with mufflers;

     With the above mitigation measures, the project will avoid nighttime construction as much
as possible, and the impact of daytime construction noise on close-range environmental
protection can be reduced from moderate to small.

8.5 Impacts of Solid Waste Pollution
     (1) Impact analysis
     Solid waste during the construction period, mainly including domestic waste, construction
waste, construction spoil and so on.

     (2) Control measures
     Earthwork allocation and transportation program:

        The topsoil available in the area occupied by the project should be stripped and
stockpiled separately before project construction, and topsoil stockpile protection and
management should be strengthened to ensure effective reuse;

        Balance between excavation and filling, carry out filling at the same time as
excavation to minimize repeated transportation. The total product of excavation (filling) and
the transportation distance should be the smallest value possible, i.e., the transportation route
and distance are reasonable, the transportation distance is the shortest, and the total volume of
earth transportation is the smallest;

        The allocation of earth should consider the combination of recent construction and
later utilization. When the project is staged in batches, the balance of the earth of the previous
phase should be combined with the needs of the later phases and consider the use of the
number of stacking location, so as to handy nearby allocation, the stacking location should be


                                                 83
ready for the later phases, and strive to avoid repeated excavation and transportation, when
there is a lack of earth in the previous phase, excavation can be made from the locations of the
later phases;

        After the end of construction, the construction site should be leveled in time, and the
site should be cleared thoroughly, and part of the construction waste should be used for
backfilling of the site, and the remaining part should be transported out for comprehensive
utilization.

     Solid waste pollution prevention measures:

        Construction waste such as earth, bricks, soil and concrete blocks are prioritized for
in-situ use to reduce construction waste discharge;

        Unusable construction waste will be collected by the contractors and transported in a
timely manner to the construction waste landfill designated by the designated ecological and
environmental authorities for safe landfilling, and no solid waste shall be discarded or scattered
along the way during transportation;

        Construction waste should be sealed and covered during temporary storage and
transportation to prevent scattering into the environment;

        Solid waste shall not be discharged freely into Lake Aha Reservoir, the Baiyan River,
the Youyu River, and other rivers;

        Construction sites that generate and need to temporarily store hazardous wastes should
set up hazardous waste storage points or temporary storage rooms in accordance with the
requirements of the "Pollution Control Standards for the Storage of Hazardous Wastes"
(GB18597-203), take measures to protect against wind, rain, sunlight, corrosion, seepage, and
interception, and make good markings, and be equipped with emergency disposal materials for
leakage. Hazardous wastes should be collected in a categorized manner, sealed and packed, and
stored temporarily in the hazardous waste storage facility. Hazardous waste storage facilities
should take technical and management measures to prevent the entry of unrelated personnel;

        Construction areas set up temporary garbage collection boxes at fixed points, and the
collected domestic waste is handled in the nearest villages and towns according to their transfer
and disposal systems;




                                                 84
        Strengthen construction management and staff training. Strengthen the identification
of hazardous waste during the collection of construction waste, and standardize the collection,
temporary storage, disposal and related management of construction waste and hazardous
waste. Standardize the placement of domestic waste, appoint special personnel to regularly
inspect the construction site, if non-standard placement of waste is found, it should be cleaned
up and collected, and on-site landfilling or burning of garbage should be strictly prohibited.

     After taking the above control measures, all kinds of solid wastes generated during the
construction period will not be discharged into the environment, and the risk of causing
environmental pollution is very small.

8.6 Pollution Impacts under Accident Conditions
    (1) Impact analysis
     Risks of surface water, soil, and groundwater contamination:

     The project greenway site is accompanied by the reservoir shoreline, and the route is
located in Lake Aha National Wetland Park. If an accident occurs during the transportation,
loading and unloading of paint, oil, asphalt and other construction materials, resulting in
material leakage, the leaked material may diffuse into the surface water body, resulting in
pollution; if the road surface is not hardened and paved, the leaked material may also be
infiltrated, resulting in soil and groundwater pollution.

     In case of accidents such as leakage of machinery and equipment, temporary storage of
paints, oils and other liquid chemicals, etc., and on the ground with leakage which have no
anti-seepage measures, the leaked materials can directly infiltrate into the soil, resulting in
contamination of soil and groundwater.

     Impacts on wildlife:

     Spills of diesel fuel, motor oil or other chemicals may also affect the growth of vegetation
in the contaminated area, or even cause death, if they cause contamination of surface water, soil
and groundwater; wildlife may be poisoned if they come into direct contact with the spilled
material, or if they drink contaminated water or eat plants in the contaminated area.

    (2) Control measures
        For transportation projects, clauses to prevent spilling of road construction materials
(e.g., asphalt concrete, etc.) during transportation should be specified in the contract;




                                                  85
         Construction vehicles, construction machinery should use qualified equipment, with
regular maintenance to ensure that there is no dripping. Maintenance of machinery and
equipment should rely on the neighboring towns and cities mechanic workshop as much as
possible, to avoid the maintenance process of oil dripping that causes soil pollution. If it is
necessary to maintain at the operation site, trays and other leakage trapping measures should be
established to prevent oil from dripping into the soil and causing pollution;

         Temporary storage sites for paint, oil and other liquid chemical construction materials,
liquid hazardous waste should take measures to prevent seepage and leakage, such as
hardening the warehouse floor and skirt, or the use of secondary containers. Regular
inspections are carried out to prevent leakage;

         In the event of oil or chemical spillage, emergency disposal measures will be taken;
after the completion of on-site disposal, corresponding restoration work will be carried out
depending on the environmental pollution or ecological damage caused by the accident;

         Prepare emergency response plans for oil and chemical spills and conduct regular
drills.

      With the above control measures in place, the risk of leakage accidents, environmental
pollution or ecological damage from construction activities is low.

8.7 Occupational Health and Safety and Risks for Construction Workers
     (1) Impact analysis
      There are risks to the occupational health and safety of personnel during the construction
of ecological protection and restoration activities and civil works activities.

      Occupational health and safety risks for construction workers can be effectively prevented
by wearing appropriate labor protection gear, establishing compliance with standard operating
procedures, and strengthening training and management.

     (2) Mitigation measures
         Provide OHS training to all new workers and keep records of the training. They are
introduced to the basic rules of work on the construction site, the rules of personal protection
and how to avoid harming other workers, and are made aware of the occupational health and
safety hazards to which they are exposed, as well as of the use of the appropriate labor
protection equipment, and the emergency response measures;




                                                  86
        Provide construction personnel with personal protective equipment that meets the
requirements of their specific job. All personnel entering the construction site shall wear
personal protective equipment as required;

        Regular maintenance of construction equipment to avoid breakdowns during use;
close, disconnect, isolate, shut down machinery with exposed and shrouded moving parts and
machinery with energy storage (e.g., compressed air, electric components) during maintenance;

        Noisy machinery operators on the site, should be equipped with the necessary
earmuffs and other noise protection items, with strict implementation of operating procedures,
and the use of over-service machinery should be prohibited;

        Install vibration dampening pads or dampening devices on vibrating equipment and
limit operating hours per shift to avoid overexposure;

        The construction site shall have firefighting facilities or be provided with fire
extinguishing equipment and regularly maintained, which shall be maintained in good
condition and placed in an easily accessible place;

        Hazardous areas (e.g., distribution rooms, compressor rooms), equipment, materials,
safety measures, emergency exits, etc. should be appropriately marked with safety signs;

        Display safety signs on all electrical equipment and cords. Inspect all wires, cables,
and hand-held power tools for damaged or exposed wires. Determine the maximum allowable
voltage for hand-held tools according to the manufacturer's recommendations. All electrical
equipment used in wet (or potentially wet) environments should be double insulated or
grounded;

        Road upgrading and other project activities located along village and town roads shall
investigate the construction site and its vicinity for the presence of underground pipelines,
fiber-optic cables, above-ground transmission and transformation lines and other facilities. If
they exist, advice should be sought from the appropriate authorities and safety measures should
be taken before construction;

        Install protective fencing around the edges of hazardous areas. Also, equip workers
with fall protection devices (including safety belts and distance limiting ropes);




                                                 87
            Plan and zone vehicular traffic, machinery operation, and walking areas, control of
vehicular traffic through one-way traffic rules, establish speed limits, and direct traffic by
trained signalmen (wearing visible undershirts or jackets) at the site;

            Ensure personnel wear visible undershirts to increase visibility when working or
walking in heavy machinery operating areas;

            Ensure that mobile equipment is fitted with a back-up alarm;

            Ensure that all buildings on the construction site are in good condition. Temporary
buildings should be safe, sturdy, able to withstand inclement weather, adequately lighted, and
insulated from some noise and dust;

            Excavation such as interceptor pipeline or station foundation should follow the
designed slope ratio layer by layer, and attention should be paid to strengthening the support
for the operations on the site;

            For project sites where natural disasters such as flash floods, landslides and floods
may occur, evacuation routes and shelters should be planned and training should be provided to
all staff;

            Develop a reporting system for potential safety accidents so that construction workers
can promptly report unsafe or unhealthy work situations and stay out of harm's way. Develop
an emergency response plan for accidents (including an evacuation plan), with drills every
year;

            Compliant first aid equipment shall be available at the construction site.

8.8 Traffic Safety Risks
     (1) Impact analysis
        During the construction of the project, due to material transportation, personnel traffic,
etc., the regional traffic flow increases, and may involve the temporary occupation or closure of
part of the road, and the upgrading and reconstruction of Jinzhu Road, Jinshan Road, Shangba
Access Road, and C416 involve the occupation of roads, bringing additional risks of traffic
safety to the villages and townships where the construction sites are located and the village and
township residents and staff along the material transportation route. The contractors’
transportation vehicles should be maintained on a regular basis, and training to the drivers
should be enhanced, and improve the safety in conjunction with the maintenance of facilities
on the affected road sections and the speed limit measures on the road sections through the


                                                     88
villages and townships. The traffic and road safety impact analysis are detailed in the Social
Impact Assessment Report.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        All new employees are provided with occupational health and safety training, which
introduces the basic rules of work on the construction site, the rules of personal protection, and
how to avoid harming other workers, so that they understand the occupational health and safety
hazards they face, as well as the use of the corresponding labor protection equipment, and
emergency response measures;

        Provide appropriate training for construction personnel and drivers of construction
machinery and construction vehicles, and conduct regular maintenance of construction
machinery;

        When it is necessary to close or partially occupy a public road, listen to the opinions
of the surrounding residents and formulate a temporary traffic plan to facilitate their daily
travel. It should be reported to the local traffic management department for approval before
construction, and the surrounding community should be informed of the situation and the
temporary rerouting arrangements, and sufficient signs, isolation, speed limits and other traffic
control measures should be set up around the site and the area occupied by the construction to
ensure the safety of the people coming and going. If necessary, appoint a person responsible for
directing vehicles in and out of the construction site and maintaining traffic order. Problems
affecting traffic are found and rectified immediately.

8.9 Physical Cultural Resources
     Based on the on-site verification, it was found that no known cultural heritage or
archaeological sites have been identified within the project area. However, construction
activities may disturb unknown subsurface cultural remains. To address this issue, the PIU and
the contractors shall be required to establish a chance find procedure for the discovery of
tangible cultural resources: if any cultural relics are found during construction, in accordance
with Article 32 of the Law of the People's Republic of China on the Protection of Cultural
Relics, (1) stop the construction work; (2) protect the site and report it to the cultural relics
management department of Guiyang City immediately; (3) adjust the construction plan in
accordance with the opinion of the cultural relics management department ; and (4) resume
construction only after the approval of the cultural relics management department. For details,
see Annex 3 - Chance Find Procedures (CFP) for Cultural Heritage.



                                                 89
9. Analysis of Environmental Risks and Impacts during Operation

9.1 Analysis of Positive Environmental Benefits
9.1.1 Reducing carbon emissions contributes to mitigating and combating climate change
     Located in the middle and upper reaches of the Yangtze River and the Pearl River,
Guizhou is an important ecological barrier between the two rivers, with extensive development
of karst landforms, many mountainous areas and a generally fragile ecological environment.
Against the background of global warming, from 1961 to 2021, the annual average temperature
in Guizhou Province increased with an overall upward trend. Persistent hot weather leads to
degradation of wetland ecosystems, increased instability of forest ecosystems, and threats to
biodiversity. The project applies nature-based solutions to reduce carbon emissions and
increase carbon sequestration through ecological restoration, construction of public
transportation facilities, and improvement of road network to improve transportation efficiency,
etc. The implementation of this project can help carbon peaking and carbon neutrality,
scientifically implement the action of climate change adaptation, and maximize regional
climate resilience.

9.1.2 Ecosystem restoration, biodiversity conservation and improved ecosystem stability
     The construction content of this project contains restoration and improvement of urban
wetlands, 4.2 mu of Baiyan River wetlands, 1.1 mu of Youyu River, 1.8 mu of Caichong Gully
wetlands, 1.2 mu of Lanni Gully wetlands. The construction content includes (1) surface
cleaning, riverbed renovation and shaping, planting emergent plants, water-submerging plants,
trees, shrubs; (2) bird habitat protection, located in the northwestern part of the park in the area
of Kailong Village and the southern part of the park with three river inlets into the reservoir
and the area of Xiaoche River, with a total protection area of 53.29 hectares; (3) river water
ecology restoration and shoreline restoration and other projects. Through targeted protection
and restoration of the Lake Aha wetland ecosystem, strengthening biodiversity protection,
carrying out monitoring and assessment of the Lake Aha wetland, effectively protecting rare
and endangered species and ecosystems in the basin, and promoting the restoration and growth
of biodiversity to maintain the ecological balance of the basin and the capacity for sustainable
development.

     In addition, project activities include monitoring and management of exotic species,
removal of invasive alien species, and monitoring and protection activities for key protected




                                                  90
wildlife, which will contribute to the conservation of species, maintain the ecological security
of Lake Aha, and improve the stability of the ecosystem.

9.1.3 Improvement of wastewater treatment facilities around Lake Aha to improve water
      quality in Lake Aha
     Problems such as "overflowing, bubbling, dripping and leaking" of domestic wastewater
from residents in the basin have led directly to the discharge of some untreated wastewater
directly into the river, which has become one of the main sources of water pollution. The
wastewater not only contains a lot of organic matter, nitrogen and phosphorus and other
nutrients, but also may contain heavy metals, toxic and hazardous substances, posing a serious
threat to the water quality of the river. The project builds a new interception pipeline around
the lake of about 22km, which collects domestic wastewater and relies on the existing Erqiao
Wastewater Treatment Plant and Xiaohe Wastewater Treatment Plant for treatment. 9.8km of
interception mains will be built in Baiyan River and Youyu River basin, with 17.8km of branch
pipeline connected to the households, 8 wastewater treatment stations, which will collect the
wastewater from Wushan Village, Gonggu Village, Datong Village, and Xuechang Village for
centralized   treatment   and    then   for   agricultural   irrigation.   The   dredging   and
rainwater-wastewater separation for Lanni Gully and wastewater interception and upgrading
for Xiaoche River under the project can realize effective collection and treatment of wastewater,
reduce direct wastewater discharge, and increase the regional wastewater treatment rate from
50% to 100% and the centralized wastewater treatment rate from 30% to 70%. In addition, the
construction of river buffer zone and estuarine wetland, with the plant community's culturing
and purifying effects, will effectively intercept the surrounding agricultural surface pollution
and rural wastewater, and effectively reduce pollutants and thus improve the water quality of
the basin.

9.1.4 Popularization of science, outdoor museums, etc., to raise residents' awareness of
      environmental protection
     In the process of wetland protection and park construction, through various forms of
popular science propaganda and education, not only the connotation and level of wetland
ecological culture will be enriched and improved, but also the surrounding masses will
establish the awareness of caring for wetlands and protecting wetlands. The surrounding
masses will be guided to protect the wetland environment as the conscious behavior and
honorable responsibility of every person.




                                                91
9.2 Environmental Risks and Negative Environmental Impacts
9.2.1 Water environment impact analysis
    (1) Impact analysis
     Wastewater during the operation period of the project is mainly domestic wastewater
produced by tourists and staff, and the stations are equipped with toilets (17 seats) and mobile
ecological toilets as needed. The domestic wastewater is purified and treated through integrated
wastewater treatment facilities, so that the treated water quality reaches the secondary standard
in the national "Comprehensive Wastewater Discharge Standard (GB8978～ 1996)", and the
treated water is recycled or used as greening water in the park.

     Baiyan River Basin and Youyu and Basin Rural Water Pollution Prevention and Control
Project will take the domestic wastewater of 3,336 people in 4 administrative villages and 8
natural stockaded village groups in Jiu’an Township in a relatively centralized way and collect
the domestic wastewater into the wastewater treatment station (pre-treatment+ micro-power
bio-filter process) to be treated to meet the standard and then used for agricultural irrigation.
The construction of the project can improve the regional wastewater treatment capacity,
improve the collection pipeline network, and have an obvious positive effect on the
improvement of the water quality of Lake Aha. It will not adversely affect the surface water
environment.

    (2) Mitigation measures
         The project's greenway works set up 17 public toilets, all of which are arranged along
the route and in the stations, with supporting with auxiliary wastewater collection and
treatment systems to ensure that wastewater in the area is properly treated and does not pollute
the river, lake and the environment;

         Strengthen the environmental protection education for the residents of the
communities around the wetland park, establish and enhance their environmental protection
awareness, and control and reduce the environmental pollution of the basin.

9.2.2 Atmospheric impact analysis
    (1) Impact analysis
        Vehicle exhaust: the construction content of this project includes greenway , municipal
roads and highways and ecological restoration works, of which the ecological restoration
works do not emit air pollutants and can be carried out for ecological system upgrading to
enhance its carbon sequestration function. The greenway is only for pedestrians and



                                                 92
non-motorized vehicles, and does not emit air pollutants, so the main air pollution during the
operation period of the project is automobile exhaust from road operation.

     Malodorous gas from domestic wastewater treatment stations: the temporary storage
of sludge from project wastewater treatment stations may produce malodorous gas.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        Vehicle exhaust:

        According to the Regulations on Prevention and Control of Air Pollution in Guizhou
Province, it is prohibited to drive a motor vehicle that fails the air pollutant emission test or
emits black smoke and other clearly visible pollutants while traveling on the road

        Priority is given to new models of urban public transportation vehicles that use
environment-friendly fuels such as electricity and natural gas to control pollutant emissions;

        For the oil-fueled car, the quality of oil should be strictly controlled, and the
high-quality fuel should be used to reduce the emission of pollutants; the cars with poor
performance or the cars to be eliminated soon should be retrofitted with tailpipe purification
devices, the tailpipe emissions should be regularly monitored by the traffic authorities, and the
cars that fails to emit exhaust up to standard are strictly prohibited to the road;
        Develop an operation and maintenance plan for the project's road works, strengthen
operation and maintenance, and keep the roads clean and in good operating condition;
        Combined with greening on both sides of the road, plant street trees to reduce dust;
        Odour:
        The domestic wastewater treatment station adopts adsorption, masking and other
measures to reduce the impact of malodorous gases on the environment.

9.2.3 Noise
    (1) Impact analysis
     Traffic noise:

     Noise sources during the operation period of the project involve fixed sound sources
(including 5 integrated pumping stations in Jinzhu area, 1 wastewater lifting pump station in
eastern Aha Village area, 1 lifting pump station in northern Caoba area, and 2 wastewater
pump houses in Xiaoche River) and mobile sound sources such as newly constructed and
reconstructed roads and highways.
