     Social life noise:

     The wilderness nature museum and the greenway around the lake are deep into the natural
environment, and social noise generated by visitor excursions, if excessive, may interfere with
normal wildlife activities, as described in Section 10.4.2.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        Traffic noise:
        Select low-noise vehicles, low-noise road surfaces and other measures for prevention
and control;
        Gradually improve and raise the emission standards for motor vehicle noise;
implement a system of regular testing of motor vehicle noise, and impose mandatory repairs on
vehicles until the noise meets the standards before they are allowed to travel on the road; and
eliminate noisy vehicles;
        Strictly limit the speed of traffic on sensitive roads, and strictly control the speeding
behavior of large vehicles at night;
        Install no-honking and speed limit signs on the road in the town area to reduce the
environmental impact of vehicle horns;
        The management of road surface and facilities along the road should be strengthened
during the use of the road, the damaged road surface should be repaired in time, and sufficient
levelness and cleanliness should be maintained to reduce traffic noise;
        Strictly implement environmental noise monitoring program, track and monitor
sensitive points along the route of the sound environment, once the project's excessive impact
on the sound environment along the sensitive points is found, the contractors should then take
reasonable engineering measures for noise reduction, to ensure that the quality of the sound
environment along the sensitive points can meet the requirements of the corresponding
functional areas.
        Social life noise:
        Select low-noise equipment for wastewater lifting pump; adopt acoustic control
measures such as sound absorption, muffling, sound insulation, vibration damping, etc.; and
place the sound source underground and semi-underground;
        The strength of social noise source from the tourists in the scenic area is generally
60~70dB(A), which can meet the corresponding standard requirements of "Sound Environment
Quality Standard" (GB3096-2008) after 10~30m distance attenuation;

     The impact of social noise on of the neighboring community during the operation period
is relatively small, which can be further reduced by strengthening science popularization and
                                                  96
education facilities, strengthening the management of outdoor open space, providing tips to the
tourists, and controlling the flow of visitors to reduce the strong source of social noise.

9.2.4 Solid waste
     (1) Impact analysis
     Solid wastes during the operation phase of the project are mainly domestic waste
generated during the operation phase of the wetland park, as well as sludge generated from the
operation of the wastewater treatment stations (8).

     Domestic waste:

    During the operation period of this project, the greenway tourists, visitors to the science

popularization and education facilities and staff will generate domestic waste. If the domestic waste is

directly discharged into the environment, it may cause water pollution and landscape damage.

     Sludge from wastewater treatment stations:

     The rural water pollution prevention and control works for Baiyan River and Youyu River
basins will build 8 new wastewater treatment stations, using pre-treatment+ micro-power
biofilter process, and the treatment process will generate sludge, some of which are retained
suspended substances, or biological sludge discharged by the biological treatment system,
which must be properly handled and disposed of, and will cause secondary pollution otherwise.

     In summary, the solid waste disposal and utilization during the project's operation period
are clearly defined, and the risk of waste entering environment and causing environmental
pollution is relatively small if the management is strengthened. However, during the operation
period, the waste generated by the tourists and patrol of greenway and nature museum and the
staff of field investigation and monitoring will be scattered in the wilderness, the collection
work will be affected by the construction of garbage collection facilities and the environmental
protection awareness of field staff and tourists and other subjective factors, such as the absence
of infrastructure or the non-standard placement of garbage by the staff and tourists may let the
garbage into the natural environment, resulting in damage to the landscape and environmental
pollution. Some of the plastic products and other difficult-to-biodegrade substances can exist in
the environment for a long time, and migrate through nature and animals, causing continuous
landscape damage, and may also be eaten by wild animals, causing health hazards. Therefore,
the risk of solid waste pollution during the operation period is moderate.

     (2) Mitigation measures
         Domestic waste:

                                                    97
       Outdoor museums and other outdoor excursion areas where visitors are introduced
should be reasonably equipped with garbage cans. The resting platforms, pavilions and other
places are equipped with garbage, and garbage cans are set up on the greenway around the lake
according to a certain spacing;

       Specialized garbage collection points are set up in the wetland park for centralized
storage and transfer of domestic garbage of the project, and specialized garbage transport
trucks are equipped;

       Strengthen the environmental protection propaganda to tourists, mobilize tourists to
take the initiative, regulate the garbage disposal, and prevent garbage from entering the natural
environment and causing pollution;

       Outdoor excursion areas are regularly patrolled by specialized personnel to collect
trash scattered in the wild environment in a timely manner to prevent further spread;

       Provide pre-service and regular environmental protection training to the patrol,
maintenance and other field staff in the operation period, collect and bring back waste
packaging, paper, plastics and other non-biomass garbage, waste generated during the field
work to domestic garbage collection points in the villages and towns, and prohibit direct
disposal in the field environment;

        Sludge:

       The small amount of sludge generated should be stored in the sludge storage tank and
transported away by the sludge suction trucks arranged by sludge disposal center or large
wastewater treatment plant for treatment and landfill up to standard. The sludge storage tank is
well protected against seepage, rain and other measures;

     After taking the above control measures, the solid waste generated by the project will
have less impact on the environment.

9.2.6 Pesticide management
     According to the FSR, this project does not use pesticides in the alien species cleanup and
later maintenance works, with the main focus on prevention, based on forest art measures, it
makes full use of nature's control factors of pests and diseases and creates conditions
unfavorable to the occurrence and development of pests and diseases, strengthens the
forecasting of outbreak and monitoring of the hazards according to the different biological
characteristics and habitats of the pests, and reasonably applies the complementary and
mutually reinforcing measures based on local conditions, such as biological, physical and
                                                98
chemical, etc., to control the pests at a tolerable level by coordinating the measures as much as
possible to avoid killing natural enemies and polluting the environment.

     If subsequent biological control cannot effectively control pests and diseases, when
pesticides need to be used, it is necessary to choose the highly effective, low-toxicity and
low-residue chemical pesticides, and at the same time to adopt safe application methods to
reduce the residues of chemical pesticides in the soil or water environment.

     Strictly implement the contact and reporting system for forestry pest monitoring and
forecasting to ensure early detection, reporting and disposal of disasters and epidemics.

     Efforts should be made to grasp quarantine inspection and interception, and to prevent the
spread of harmful organisms. Focus should be put on the control of forestry pest epidemics at
the source, the quarantine of origin and the quarantine inspection of shipments should be
regarded as the mainstay, especially focusing on strengthening the quarantine inspection of
plants and their products that are capable of carrying dangerous forestry pests, and further
increasing the intensity of quarantine law enforcement, so as to investigate and deal with cases
of quarantine violations in accordance with the law, and to effectively prevent the spread of
harmful organisms.

     Environmental protection is one of the core elements of the safe use of pesticides. Special
attention should be paid to the protection of water sources when applying pesticides, avoiding
the application of pesticides near rivers, lakes and reservoirs to prevent pesticides from
polluting water bodies. Isolation zones or buffer zones should be established to prevent
pesticides from flowing into water bodies and affecting aquatic organisms and human health.
The waste should be disposed of after pesticide application, such as pesticide packaging and
residual liquid, etc., which should be recycled and treated in a harmless way in accordance with
environmental protection requirements to avoid environmental pollution. In ecologically
sensitive areas, such as wildlife habitats and ecologically fragile areas, stricter restrictions on
the use of pesticides should be adopted to minimize the impact on the ecosystem and protect
biodiversity and the ecological environment.

     Personal protection of applicators is also an important part of ensuring the safe use of
pesticides. Applicators should wear protective clothing, gloves, masks and goggles and other
personal protective equipment to avoid pesticide contact with the skin, eyes and respiratory
tract. Before applying pesticides, they should read the instructions in detail, to master the
correct application and safe operation procedures. After the application of pesticides, their
exposed parts of the body should be timely cleaned, with change of work clothes, to avoid

                                                  99
secondary pollution. The health and safety of applicators will be protected through strict
personal protection measures.

     Storage and transportation of pesticides are also important to ensure their safe use.
Pesticides should be stored in cool, dry, ventilated special warehouses, avoiding direct sunlight
and high temperatures. The storage area should be equipped with obvious warning signs to
prevent misuse and abuse. When transporting pesticides, special vehicles should be used to
ensure that the packaging is intact and prevent leakage and contamination. The transportation
process should comply with relevant safety regulations to ensure safe transportation. Scientific
treatment of pesticide residues is also one of the key measures for the safe use of pesticides.
According to the degradation characteristics of pesticides and the growth cycle of crops, the
time of application should be rationalized to ensure that the pesticide residues comply with
national standards at the time of harvest of agricultural products. The safety intervals should be
followed to avoid exceeding pesticide residues and to ensure the quality and safety of
agricultural products.

     Through the above measures, the negative impact of pesticide use on the environment and
human health can be effectively reduced, the safety and prevention and control effects of
pesticide use can be improved, and the sustainable development of agriculture and forestry can
be guaranteed. At the same time, it will promote the standardization and scientization of
pesticide management, enhance the overall level of pest control, and provide a solid guarantee
for the realization of sustainable agriculture and forestry development.




                                                 100
10 Ecological Impact Analysis

     The PMO has engaged Guiyang City Transportation Planning Survey Design Institute Co.,
Ltd to carry out more detailed Domestic Environmental Assessment (DEIA), including special
ecological assessment, and the approval from Guiyang Municipal EEB has been obtained on
June 4th 2025 (ZHUHUANBIAO [2025] No.87).

     In conjunction with the survey results and conclusions in the Special Ecological
Assessment Report, this report comprehensively analyzed the potential impacts caused by the
project implementation, and proposed corresponding feasible mitigation measures, in order to
minimize the adverse impacts on the ecological environment.

10.1 Pest and Disease Management Risks
    (1) Risk analysis
     The construction of the forest vegetation restoration area on the north shore of Lake Aha
involved in this project, the ecological and botanical landscape restoration along the greenway,
the water ecological restoration, the restoration of the bird habitats, and the greening on both
sides of the road will introduce seedlings.

     During the construction period, especially the restoration works of forest vegetation in
the areas with high sensitivity such as the national wetland park, if diseased or pest -affected
seedlings are introduced, they will not only impact the areas with revegetation, but also
further influence the forest around the project area, and further damage the ecological
balance of wetland, influence the wetland functions, and lower the quality of ecological
habitat.

     In addition, there are also pest and disease risks during the operation of the project.
For instance, the use of pesticides for pest control during the nursery and maintenance periods
will kill beneficial natural enemies of pests while killing the pests, resulting in a reduction of
biodiversity and an imbalance of species in the project area. Also, the application of pesticides
may directly harm wildlife.

     Sensitivity/Importance: Lake Aha Biodiversity Survey identifies the secondary protected
plant golden buckwheat, located in the Jinzhong River basin, which is outside of the project's
area of impact, with a moderate species sensitivity.

     Impact level: the construction period is relatively short, the impact area is limited, the
project design stage has considered the scientific configuration of tree species to ensure the
ability of the forest stand to resist pests and diseases, through strict selection of seedlings,

                                                 101
quarantine inspection and other measures during the construction period, the introduction of
plants with pests and diseases will be avoided, therefore a small impact is expected.

    (2) Mitigation measures
     In this project, the greening engineering design scheme for each ecological protection and
restoration activity and civil works activity will be based on the established laws and
regulations on pest control in China, and the tree species will be scientifically configured
without pure forests, so as to improve the ability of resistance to pests and diseases through
species diversity, and to reduce the incidence of pests and diseases in the forestry activities
under the project. Wetland pest and disease control will adhere to the principles of prevention,
early treatment, small treatment, and controlling the spread of pests and diseases, actively
adopt advanced control technology, and adhere to biological control as the main prevention and
control measure, to nip pests and diseases in the bud. The prevention and control work that
uses pests to treat pests and uses fungi to treat fungi will be increased. The specific principles
are as follows:

        Scientific configuration of tree species with the goal of creating suitable habitats, with
the combination of the diversity of tree species, seed sources, genotypes and ages to enrich the
diversity of plant species;

        Forest land restoration and greening works should be suitable for the right places and
the right trees, with a reasonable mix of tree species, and strict control over the proportion of
the same tree species and the scale of continuous planting;

        The construction design plan balances cut and fill locally as much as possible to
reduce the risk of introducing pests and diseases associated with the transportation of earth and
rock over long distances.

        Procurement of seedlings strictly follows the "two certificates and one signature"
system, and selects the strong seedlings, healthy seedlings, local native species that pass the
quarantine for planting and cultivation, to eliminate the spread of pests and diseases from the
source, and improve the survival rate of seedlings;

        All seedlings, seeds, flowers, etc. shall be quarantined in accordance with the
requirements of the regulations before being transferred, and the use of plants and seeds with
dangerous pests and diseases for transplanting and planting is prohibited;

        Personnel and vehicles from pest and disease infested areas are inspected and
quarantined before entering the project area;

                                                 102
       Protection of birds and natural enemies of insects, most of wetland birds are
insectivorous birds, and fowling should be strictly prohibited, to provide conditions for birds to
survive and reproduce;

       The most effective way to protect natural enemies of insects is to protect the
ecological environment on which they depend for their survival, with specific measures such as
rationalizing the operation and banning the use of chemical agents, and prohibiting the use of
chemical pesticides to clear weeds from the ground;

       Special personnel should be appointed for the prevention and control work of pests
and diseases to strengthen the monitoring of forest land within the construction area. When the
pines that are suspiciously withered or have the color of their needles changed are discovered,
they should be reported to the Park Management Office and handled by the special personnel;

       The construction and operation personnel should be made aware of the Rules of Plant
Quarantine, the Rules of Prevention and Control of Forestry Pests and Diseases, and other laws
and regulations and knowledge on prevention and control, and their perception on the hazards
and the prevention and control work of forestry pests should be enhanced.

     Measures are taken to reduce the level of risk to an "acceptable level".

10.2      Risk of Introducing Alien Species
     The site survey revealed that there are 22 exotic plant species in the project area, eight of
which are invasive: Pontederia crassipes, Bidens pilosa, Ageratum conyzoides, Erigeron
canadensis, Erigeron annuus, Ipomoea purpurea, Symphyotrichum subulatum, and
Alternanthera philoxeroides.




    (1) Risk analysis
     The works under the project which involve the introduction of seedlings include
ecological protection and restoration activities (including forest vegetation restoration, water

                                                 103
ecological restoration, shoreline restoration, and ecological wetland construction or upgrading),
and greening works in some civil works.

     When designing the introduction of seedlings, inappropriate selection of tree species may
lead to invasive alien species. Some of the species introduced as greening or ornamental plants
are highly expansive and may affect the local ecosystem and then jeopardize local biodiversity.

     Meanwhile, soil from construction vehicles, machinery and equipment, and construction
workers' clothing may carry seeds of invasive species. Seeds that may enter the project area
with vehicles, personnel, and machinery and equipment during construction could introduce
invasive species or result in the spread of invasive species already present in the project area to
a wider area.

     Sensitivity/Importance: The project involves ecologically sensitive areas such as the red
line of ecological protection, and the habitat sensitivity is substantial, and the project area
identifies a variety of rare wild animals and plants, so the species sensitivity is high.

     Impact level: the construction period is relatively short, the impact area is limited. In the
meantime, the project design stage has considered the scientific configuration of tree species,
native species are preferred for forest vegetation restoration, to avoid the introduction of exotic
tree species, so the impact is expected to be small.

     (2) Mitigation measures
     China has formulated laws, regulations and management systems related to biosafety,
plant quarantine, and exotic species management, and the principles of these laws and
regulations have been incorporated in the design of activities related to this project,
specifically:

        Selection of tree species for ecological restoration should be high-quality native tree
species, and excellent seedlings, strong seedlings from local nurseries should be used as many
as possible for replanting, to avoid long-distance transportation to bring in exotic species;

        The construction design plan balances cut and fill locally as much as possible to
reduce the risk of introducing exotic species during the long-distance transportation of earth
and rock;

        During the construction process, a special person is appointed to be responsible for the
quarantine and nursery of seedlings, as well as seedling management, and audit and checking
of seedling purchase, to ensure that the seedlings planted in the project are not exotic species
and at the same time do not carry exotic species;
                                                   104
        All seedlings, seeds, flowers, etc. should be quarantined in accordance with the
requirements of the regulations before being transferred to strictly prevent the introduction of
foreign species;

        Persons and vehicles from alien species hazard areas should be inspected and
quarantined, etc., before entering the project area;

        Training of construction workers on the hazards of alien species and preventive
measures should be provided;

        Strengthen the monitoring and investigation of the distribution and number of invasive
alien species, regularly assess the degree of their invasion and the harm they do to the
ecosystem, and, based on the results of the assessment, take timely physical control measures
such as removing and harvesting, and inhibit the spread of invasive alien species in conjunction
with the restoration of native species.

     Overall, the risk of invasion of alien species under the project is quite low.

10.3      Potential Impacts on the Wetland Park
    (1) Impact analysis
     The project construction involves the restoration area and conservation area of the wetland
park. Specifically, the adverse impacts on Lake Aha National Wetland Park mainly come from
the process of road construction. For instance, the project construction will generate certain
amount of exhaust, wastewater, and noise, which will cause certain impacts on the ecological
environment. Meanwhile, the direct occupation of land and construction activities of the
project may damage the existing landscape environment and change the hydrological
conditions, and then impact the habitats of wetland organisms, causing the reduction of
biodiversity. In addition, the construction may also occupy or change the leisure and
recreational facilities and rest space in the wetland park, and impact the visitors’ leisure
experience.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        The project routing should avoid wetlands, and if it is not possible to avoid them, it
should minimize their occupation and take necessary measures to mitigate the adverse impacts
on the ecological functions of wetlands;

        Combined with the current situation investigation, targeted ecological restoration
techniques, such as artificial wetland and ecological embankment, are adopted to restore and
rebuild the aquatic ecosystem;

                                                  105
       Green the greenway retaining walls with green vine plants or decorative structures to
increase the harmony of the landscape;

       Enhance the landscape design of bridges within ecologically sensitive areas and
harmonize bridge elevations with water levels;

       Strictly control the scope of construction, minimize the occupation of wetlands, and
strictly implement wetland protection measures;

       For the sensitive area sections involving wetland habitats, bird tracking and
monitoring should be strengthened during construction, and the targeted protection program
should be improved according to the habitat activities of protected birds;

       Strengthen the deployment and comprehensive utilization of engineering earth and
stone and reduce the amount of spoil and spoil ground from the source. Topsoil is stripped and
preserved before construction, and ecological restoration or replanting is carried out after
construction. Temporarily occupied wetlands will be restored to their size and ecological
conditions in a timely manner after construction;

       Wetland ecological restoration uses native species, and the introduction and release of
exotic species into wetlands are prohibited; those that do need to be introduced should be
scientifically assessed and approved in accordance with the law;

       Add promotion for anti-poaching awareness on the notice boards at construction sites
(see mitigation measures in "Disturbance of Wildlife by Construction Activities");

       Strengthen wetland protection publicity and education and popularization of scientific
knowledge for construction workers to enhance the awareness of wetland protection in the
whole society;

       During the operation period, the surrounding population is encouraged to participate in
water ecological restoration, monitoring of biological taxa and cleaning of alien species;

       Biodiversity monitoring of plants, birds, mammals, amphibians, reptiles, etc to track
and protect species and prevent invasive species. The composition and diversity of plants, fish,
birds and mammals will be improved, contributing to the ecological health of the wetland.




                                                  106
10.4     Disturbance to Wildlife Habitats
10.4.1 Impacts on wildlife habitat during construction
    (1) Impact analysis
     The site investigation in the early stage and construction activities will damage the
ecosystem to some extent and indirectly affect the birds through food sources; the increase of
human activities, the noise and vibration generated by various machinery, and the partial
destruction of the habitat will have a certain impact on the birds' breeding, nest selection,
foraging, and roosting. However, due to the strong athletic ability and strong adaptability to the
environment of birds, they can avoid unfavorable external environment by flying and reduce
the impact on their roosting and foraging. In addition, the construction scope of the whole
project accounts for a relatively small proportion compared with the entire habitat of birds, and
the project siting avoids the main habitat of birds. Therefore, the entire project works will not
have significant impact on the diversity of bird species and the ecological distribution of birds
in the assessment area. In addition, the project specifically targets the restoration of bird
habitats and the restoration of wetland into the lake, water ecology, and shoreline, and the
improvement of the ecological environment can provide more food sources and habitats for
birds, and the population density of birds will be restored along with the end of the project
works.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        The project siting and routing try to avoid the north side of the forest land, Kailong
Village and the bird habitats in the southern part of the park, to prevent ecological damage
from the beginning. For the areas that cannot be avoided, adjustment or partial optimization of
siting and routing will be carried out, such as overhead trestle, natural road surface and other
measures to minimize the disturbance and damage to the habitat;

        The design increases the protection of bird habitats, strengthens the protection of bird
habitats in the Kailong Village area, sets low closed fences on the periphery, installs artificial
nesting boxes, strengthens publicity, and increases the density of patrols, reduces the
interference of peripheral production and life on birds, protects the naturalness of the habitat,
and provides a good habitat for birds;




                                                 107
                        Figure 10-1 Bird Habitat Restoration Location Map

        The design considers the impact of the project operation period on the birds in the
marshy wetland of Jinshan Village, the area will be restored and protected, and the
establishment of an ecological buffer zone between the project and the marshy wetland is
considered to minimize the disturbance to birds during the operation period of the project;

        Adhere to the idea of integrated protection and systematic management of mountains,
waters, forests, fields, lakes and grasslands, and propose ecological protection measures by
considering the Lake Aha area as a systemic whole. Adhere to the concepts of respecting nature,
adapting to nature and protecting nature, take natural restoration measures and green
restoration processes, and avoid the adverse impacts of the ecological protection measures
themselves;

        To reduce the obstruction of the road to animal activities, the height of the road edge is
reduced in the design, while the side ditch avoids the use of vertical structures, and it is
preferable to use a sloping shape or install a cover to prevent animals from falling into the
ditch.




                                                 108
                 Figure 10-2 Design Forms to Reduce Roadway Surface Obstruction

        Spatially, the construction of the project strictly controls the scope of occupation,
minimizes the construction roads in the National Wetland Park, and the construction vehicles
must operate on the planned construction roads to avoid crushing the vegetation around the
construction area and reduce the temporary occupation of land;

        Regulate the behavior of construction personnel, limit and minimize the scope of
construction operations, set up ecological warning signs in the construction area to indicate the
scope of land acquisition for the project, clarify the scope of activities of construction
personnel, prohibit construction personnel from occupying land beyond the boundary, strictly
prohibit arbitrary cutting down and destruction of vegetation outside the construction area, and
strictly control other activities outside the construction area;

        Before construction, the topsoil available in the area occupied by the project will be
stripped and stockpiled separately, and topsoil stockpile protection and management will be
strengthened to ensure effective reuse;

        If the construction adversely affects key protected wild plants, old and valuable trees,
etc., it shall optimize the siting and routing to protect them on site or relocate them, and
strengthen observation;

        Optimize the arrangement of the construction site and keep noisy operations away
from birds and other important habitats; considering that noise may have a certain impact on
the breeding rate, foraging and roosting of birds, noise reduction and vibration damping
measures should be taken during construction to minimize its impact on birds;

        From the perspective of time, because of the light and noise pollution of construction
on the foraging efficiency of birds, and even the impacts on the phenology and adaptability of
the breeding birds, the construction is required to reasonably arrange construction time, try to
avoid the peak of the activities of protected birds and their breeding period and other critical
                                                   109
activities and special protection period, and cancel or adjust the content of the project and the
construction method that produce significant adverse impacts. Attention should be paid to
reducing light and noise during the construction, and night-time construction in Lake Aha
Wetland Park is prohibited;

         Prioritize the use of eco-friendly engineering and construction technologies,
techniques and materials;

         Train construction workers on bird protection, strengthen publicity and education on
wildlife protection, add publicity signs around the construction area, strengthen management of
construction workers, and strictly prohibit hunting and killing of wildlife;

         Restore the temporarily occupied land in a timely manner after construction is
completed.

10.4.2 Impacts on wildlife habitats during operation
    (1) Positive effect analysis
Enhancement of bird habitat quality:

        The bird habitat restoration works in Kailong Village in the northwest of Lake Aha
National Wetland Park facing the mountain and the lake branch of reservoir in the south of the
park covers an area of 53.29 hectares, and through the pollution source prevention and control
and management, ecological restoration works, small habitat creation, etc., the structure and
number of plant and animal communities will be restored, the heterogeneity of bird habitat and
suitability will be improved, the diversity of birds will further enriched, and the wetland
ecosystem self-sustaining capacity will be upgraded.

     The wetland restoration, water ecology restoration and shoreline restoration work of this
project can purify water quality, nourish water sources, improve the vegetation coverage of the
project area, and improve the stability of the ecosystem. Especially for the water ecology
restoration works, by releasing benthic animals, zooplankton, fish, etc., it can increase the
variety of living organisms in the water body and improve the stability and resilience of the
ecosystem. In addition, with the steady improvement of the water ecological environment, it
can provide abundant food sources for fish and birds and attract more birds, which has
significant ecological benefits.

     In addition, the project also establishes systems for biomonitoring and bird habitat
monitoring to grasp the population dynamics of birds and habitat changes in real time, to better
carry out conservation work.

                                                 110
     Enhancement of ecosystem functions:

     The implementation of the project will increase the forest area through forest vegetation
restoration and enhance the quality of wetland ecosystems through ecological restoration,
which can improve the carbon sequestration capacity of forest and wetland ecosystems and
significantly increase carbon sinks. In addition, the project will have the following positive
effects on ecosystem service functions:

     （1） Enhancement of regulating service functions

     Forests and wetland vegetation play a role in intercepting rainwater through the forest
canopy, the shrub and grass layer, the withered leaf layer and the soil layer, reducing surface
runoff and runoff velocity and weakening the erosive force of rainfall on the surface, thus
preventing soil erosion and soil erosion. Enriching vegetation communities can also further
improve soil structure and play a role in water conservation and water purification. New and
improved forest and wetland vegetation can also purify the air, improve regional air quality,
increase carbon sinks and regulate temperature and climate.

     （2） Enhancement of cultural services

  The project carries out forest vegetation restoration, interception of pollution to improve
water quality, shoreline restoration works, and create natural cultural landscape nodes, science
education nodes, nodes with local characteristics, etc. The overall landscape of the project area
will be improved and take on the functions of science popularization and education, tourism
and sightseeing.

     （3） Enhancement of support service functions:

  By increasing the area of forests and upgrading the quality of forests and wetlands, the soil
structure can be improved, soil nutrient improvement and cycling can be promoted, and the
level of primary productivity of ecosystems can be increased, providing conditions for the
maintenance and enhancement of biodiversity. At the same time the increase in biomass, such
as vegetation, will also improve the level of oxygen supply.

     Ecological corridor construction:

     Along the northwest section of the main route of the greenway around the lake and the
concentrated and interlaced wildlife distribution area, the project provides safe passages for
wildlife activities and migratory diffusion by means of habitat bridges and habitat culverts,
reduces the impacts of the construction works on the native organisms and their habitats, and
expands the scope of the wildlife's life activities and improves the biodiversity.
                                                  111
               Figure 10-3 Location of Greenway Wildlife Corridor Around Lake Aha

    (2) Impact analysis
     The overall objective of the project is to protect and rehabilitate the Lake Aha area, and
expand the forest area, carbon sinks and other positive impacts. However, the scope of
activities during the maintenance of project greenway involves important wetlands and
ecologically sensitive areas of important habitats, which may cause some disturbance to
wildlife during the operation period. It mainly includes the following aspects:

     Sound/light/vibration disturbances to animals:

     Visitor excursions to the field sites and maintenance of newly planted vegetation during
the operational period will result in an increase in human activity within some of the habitats.
Visitor excursion activities and the corresponding increase in traffic will generate more regular
social noise, traffic noise, visual and other human disturbances, which will affect the range of
wildlife activities and interfere with animal foraging, communication and other behaviors.

     Vehicle injuries to wildlife:

     Visitor excursion activities during the operational period will result in increased traffic in
the area, and a small increase in vehicular activity for the maintenance, patrols, and other
activities for forest land restoration, with the potential for vehicle collisions and injuries to
wildlife crossing the roadway.

     The role of linear works in habitat segmentation:

     The construction of the project's greenway and access route can cause segmentation of
wildlife habitats, which will have a certain impact on the ecosystem and biodiversity of the
                                                 112
project area. However, the width of the main route of the project greenway project is 7 meters,
the access route is 2.5 meters, with some sections of the elevated walkway, so the impact on
biodiversity is relatively small, and will not cause the overall degradation of regional
ecological functions. And evasive siting, overhead greenway design, ecological corridors and
other mitigation measures are taken for the bird habitat, the impact on the ecological
environment is relatively small.

     (3) Mitigation measures
           Activities that involve wilderness education will train visitors on wildlife conservation
through the installation of informational signs, etc., and prohibit loud noises, blaring music
videos, and other noisy behaviors;

           Shrubs and trees are planted in areas where the road is suitably sloped to create buffer
zones, and wildlife presence signs are placed at the spots with traffic jam;

           Control visitor flow and touring areas as necessary;

           Low-noise drones are required for the drone monitoring program;

           Reasonably reduce the frequency of travel within the habitat, and impose a speed limit
(15km/hr) on vehicles in protected areas, habitats, and forested areas to avoid collisions or
roadkill;

           Limit patrol, monitoring, and visitor activities to daytime hours when the view is
clearer;

           Monitor the noise and light situation in bird habitats, analyze the impact of noise and
light, etc. on the activity patterns and breeding of different bird species, and take mitigation
measures;

           Intelligently adjust the brightness of lights in the wetland park area during the
operation period, and at night, it is recommended to turn off the lights of greenways and
bridges in the park to prevent disturbing the nighttime life pattern of animals;

           The south side of Lake Aha can absorb the existing beach farmland through subsidized
leases, adjust the planting of crops, and build animal canteens.

           Strengthen the management of regional fishing and grazing behavior, prohibit the use
of ground cages for fishing within the wetland park area, and encourage anglers to put the
captured native species back into the water, while invasive alien species can be taken away.



                                                    113
     By regulating the behavior of visitors, improving park management rules and regulations,
and strengthening park management, we will resolutely put an end to the digging of wild plants
and the intimidation of wildlife. The design and construction of popular science recreational
facilities should, in principle, be based on the principle that visitors should minimize
interference with the habitat of wild animals and plants.

10.5      Impacts on and Damage to Vegetation during Construction
    (1) Impact analysis
     The main route of the project greenway, access routes, stations and other activities occupy
a total of 879.7 mu of forest land and 465 mu of cultivated land, and some of the siting and
routing are located within the ecological protection red line, occupying 446.90 mu of the
ecological protection red line, and the activities of construction and personnel during the
construction period will cause damage or disturbance to some of the vegetation.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        Strengthen the environmental management during the construction period, strengthen
the environmental awareness of construction personnel, strictly control the scope of
construction activities and the width of the construction zone, optimize the construction layout
of the project, strictly limit the scope of construction activities, and reduce the occupation of
forest land;

        Works with permanent and temporary occupation of land need identify the key
protected wild plants (Emmenopterys henryi, Pterospermum heterophyllum, etc.) and old and
valuable trees in the proposed construction areas in the design stage, and take evasive measures;
Those which cannot be avoided should be relocated or protected before construction;

        Signs will be placed around the perimeter of the construction site or at relevant
locations to remind construction workers to protect the vegetation and to prohibit
encroachment on and destruction of the vegetation;

        Ecological environmental protection measures are fully considered in the construction
program, such as protective nets and grass curtains to separate vegetation from the construction
area to reduce the interference of construction on vegetation;

        Temporary works try to avoid occupying land outside the project area, especially
forest land. For example, existing roads, dirt roads and forest clearings are utilized as
construction access roads; no separate construction camps are set up, and nearby private houses
are rented;

                                                 114
            Ensure that project activities involving ecological red lines, public welfare forests and
natural forests strictly comply with relevant domestic laws and regulations. For example,
projects occupying forest land should obtain administrative licenses in accordance with the law,
and those involving public welfare forests should be transplanted or replanted off-site in
accordance with the law;

            Excavate and backfill in layers during construction, and carry out land leveling,
reploughing and replanting or ecological restoration after construction, to reduce the damage to
vegetation and the impact on wildlife.

10.6 Impacts on Aquatic Ecosystems
        (1) Impact analysis
        Benthic organisms:

        The bridges construction would have an impact on benthic organisms. The construction
content accounts for a small percentage of the project, which is works with dotted distribution
for the entire project. And according to the site survey15 mollusks include snails, river clams,
Semisulcospira snails, mussels and other taxa. At present, there is no protected species of
benthic organisms, and the short-term reduction of benthic animal species in the river section
of the project construction area will not have a big impact on the fish in the area.

        Zooplankton:

        Pollution of water bodies by wastewater, solid waste, dust and soil erosion during the
construction period may lead to a decrease in zooplankton biomass. However, with the end of
the project, the water flow returns to its natural form, and the improved water quality is
favorable for the reproduction of rotifers and planktonic crustaceans, thus increasing the
zooplankton species and biomass. Zooplankton and fish will be released because of the
project's water ecological restoration work. With the passage of time, the improvement of the
water ecological substrate environment after the construction operation and the restoration of
the regional water ecological community will form a new dynamic balance in a relatively short
period of time.

        Fish:

        According to the site survey by Beijing Jinglang, a total of 10 species of fish were found,
of which 6 species were obtained from interviews, and only the living Opsariichthys bidens
were witnessed, and no nationally protected fish or endemic rare fish were found. During the


15   Research Report on Lake Aha by Beijing Jinglang Ecological Science and Technology Co.

                                                              115
construction period, the construction of the water-related works will change the riverbank
habitat, which will have a certain negative impact on the survival of fish. However, after the
construction, the water quality of the project area will be improved, and the river water
ecological restoration and the shoreline restoration will release Rhodeus ocellatus, Rhodeus
sinensis, and Cirrhinus molitorella, the aquatic organisms will be gradually better than the
status quo because of the ecological upgrading works, and the adaptive ability of these small
fish to the environment is strong and their low requirements for living conditions will gradually
recover to the original level in a short period of time, so that the impacts on the fish resources
will be reversible.

     In conclusion, the original biomass and net production of water bodies in the project area
are not high, and these aquatic organisms are common species in the river aquatic environment,
with no protected or endangered species. Therefore, the loss of biomass and net production of
aquatic communities during the construction period is not significant, and the loss of
biodiversity caused by the project is within an acceptable range and can be gradually restored
to the original level after the construction period.

    (2) Mitigation measures
        Fish repellent measures can be taken before construction to maximize the protection of
fish resources from damage caused by water-related works;

        For the construction area where benthic animals are lost and benthic ecosystems are
damaged due to the water-related construction, restoration measures like introduction and
proliferation of benthic animals are introduced, and the benthic animals within the basin of the
construction channel or in the nearby areas are collected and sporadically released to the
dredged area, so as to introduce species and increase breeding, and to accelerate the restoration
of the benthic biological communities. The species of benthic animals to be collected and put
into the dredged area are mainly the common species in the project area, and the collection area
should be selected in the area with a large distribution of benthic organisms, and the amount of
collection should be based on the principle of not affecting the proliferation and reproduction
of benthic organisms in the collection area;

        The project will carry out ecological restoration works such as inlet wetland
restoration, aquatic ecological restoration, shoreline restoration, etc., base modification of the
basin, and release of benthic animals such as snails and mussels, zooplankton, and fish
understandings to mitigate and compensate for the impact of the implementation of the project
on benthic organisms.

                                                   116
10.7     Soil Erosion Impacts
     (1) Impact analysis
     During the construction of the project's greenway, exposed slopes may be created due to
terrain modification or excavation operations, which can easily lead to soil erosion. Activities
such as vegetation clearing and earthwork construction of the interceptor pipeline, stations, and
roadway construction on the occupied land involve earth moving operations or vegetation
clearing, and 12 bridges involve water-related construction. The occupation and surface
clearing for the project will produce bare soil and loose earth, which can exacerbate soil
erosion. The impacts of soil erosion are generally greater in areas of greater slope and during
the rainy season. See details in the project's soil and water conservation report.

     (2) Mitigation measures
        A portion of the project's greenway is elevated to minimize surface occupancy for
project construction;

        Rationalize the construction schedule and try to avoid excavation operations during
the rainy season;

        Optimize construction site layout and keep greenway construction sites as far away
from water bodies as possible;

        Water-related construction coordinates the scheduling of water levels in reservoirs to
reduce erosion from water-related construction without affecting the function of the reservoir;

        It is prohibited to collect dead branches and leaves under the forest, and the site should
be covered with dead branches, grasses, leaves, etc. after land preparation to avoid bare topsoil
and maintain soil fertility;

        Upon completion of the project, the temporarily occupied land and exposed slopes
will be greened in a timely manner, with native species as much as possible;

        Construction of water interception, drainage and other control measures are taken in
accordance with the requirements of the water conservation program, water conservation
monitoring is conducted in accordance with the requirements and commissioned with
construction supervision unit with professional qualification in soil and water conservation
project to undertake supervision tasks.




                                                  117
10.8 Analysis of Cumulative Environmental Impacts
10.8.1 Positive impacts
     The construction of this project will carry out ecological restoration of the area with rich
bird resources and much-needed habitat restoration represented by the marshy wetland of
Jinshan Village within the scope of Lake Aha Wetland Park, as well as pollution source
prevention, control and management through the interception of wastewater project around the
lake, and at the same time carry out the reconstruction of the plant community and creation of a
microhabitat, the construction of the project will improve the living environment of birds,
increase the types and numbers of birds, and improve the biodiversity of birds.

    The construction of ecological buffer zone and estuarine wetland of this project will make
use of the plant community's nutrient and purification effects and effectively intercept the
surrounding agricultural surface pollution and rural domestic wastewater, eliminate pollutants,
and enhance the ecological function of the wetland and restore its self-purification ability. In
addition, the project will also restore forest vegetation, which will enhance the functions of
forests in regulating climate, conserving soil and water, and maintaining biodiversity. The
upgrading of wetland and forest ecosystems will enhance the capacity of ecosystems to
sequester carbon.

    Combined with Guiyang City's "14th Five-Year Plan" for Ecological Environmental
Protection, the implementation of the project will effectively protect the biodiversity of the
project area, consolidate and improve the quality of the ecological environment, facilitate
Guiyang's green and low-carbon development, and enhance the city's ability to cope with
climate change.

10.8.2 Negative impacts
     The negative environmental impacts during project operation are limited to the
disturbance to wildlife by visitors, tourists and park management activities, and the impacts
due to the discharge of domestic wastewater from the wastewater treatment stations. However,
none of these impacts are significant and scattered in the lake basin. Thus, the project is not
anticipated to bring negative cumulative impacts.

     According to the "Aha Lake Basin Spatial Protection and Utilization Plan", estimated
pollutant-carrying capacity of Jinzhong River (Xiaowan River), Baiyan River, Youyu River, Caichong
Gully, Lanni Gully, etc. for COD and NH3-N is 1464.6t/a and 389.5t/a respectively, and the planning
considers the source and growth of pollution load in the basin. The planning takes into full
consideration the sources and growth trends of pollution loads in the basin, and is equipped

                                                 118
with corresponding wastewater treatment facilities, such as the late expansion of the Taici
Wastewater Treatment Plant in the Xiaoche River basin, and the construction of a new Da’ao
Wastewater Treatment Plant in the Baiyan River and Youyu River basin, which will ensure that
domestic wastewater in the basin will be properly treated, and that wastewater discharges will not
exceed the self-purification capacity of the water body, and that there will be no cumulative
environmental impacts.

      The activities under the project include park greenway, urban roads, sewers, wastewater
treatment facilities, etc, involving different responsible authorities. According to the overall
arrangements by the Guiyang Municipal Government, Guiyang Urban Construction Investment
Group Co., Ltd will serve as the implementation agency and be responsible for the overall
implementation of the project, as well as the operation and maintenance of some project
facilities, while Guiyang Municipal Traffic Commission (TC), Municipal Ecology and
Environment Bureau (EEB), Municipal Water Bureau (WB), Municipal Forestry Bureau (FB),
and Aha Lake Wetland Park will also be involved in the project implementation and operation.
Guiyang Urban Construction Investment Group Co., Ltd will hand the built assets/deliverables
over to the relevant departments for operation and maintenance in accordance with the
domestic procedures after the project completion. The detailed arrangements are shown in the

                                                  123
12. Stakeholder Engagement and Information Disclosure

     According to the Bank's Environmental and Social Policy Framework (ESF) and
Environmental Social Standard 10 - Stakeholder Engagement and Information Disclosure
(ESS10), stakeholder engagement is an inclusive process throughout the project cycle.
Effective stakeholder engagement can provide project planners and decision makers with local
knowledge, enable them to understand earlier the various potential risks that exist during
project implementation, and help to take measures in advance, thus improving the
environmental and social sustainability and acceptance of the project and contributing to
successful project design and implementation.

     During the project preparation phase, the stakeholders of the project activities were
identified, the key stakeholders were identified in relation to project activities, and their
influence on the project was assessed. Based on the stakeholder identification and analysis, a
Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) was developed for the project covering information
disclosure, stakeholder consultation and grievance redress mechanism.

     Stakeholder engagement primarily includes (but is not limited to):

     -    Establish a systematic approach to stakeholder engagement to help project
implementing agencies identify stakeholders and build and maintain constructive relationships
with them, especially those affected by the project;

     -    Inform stakeholders of the status of the project, including the purpose, nature, scale
and duration of project activities, and any potential project-related impacts and mitigation
plans;

     -    Identify stakeholder concerns, needs, complaints and grievances, and consider
stakeholder input in project design and in environmental management;

     -    Obtain stakeholder feedback on project impacts (especially environmental) and
mitigation measures;

     -    Provide channels and procedures for grievances for all types of stakeholders to
ensure that project managers can respond to and manage stakeholder complaints and
grievances in a timely manner;

     -    In the process of project decision-making and implementation, the wishes of
stakeholders are fully considered, and potential conflicts are avoided and resolved.



                                                 124
12.1      Stakeholder Identification
     The project's stakeholders fall into two categories: (1) The project's primary affected
persons. Groups and individuals who have a legal contractual relationship with the project.
These include PMO, project contractors, design agencies, project supervisors, consultants, and
households, businesses, and organizations affected by land acquisition for the project. (2) Other
Stakeholders. Groups and individuals who do not have a formal contractual relationship with
the project but are affected by the project or are able to influence the project, including project
approval government departments, project users, news media, non-governmental organizations,
and local communities and the public. Each type of stakeholders’ impact on the project and
project’s impact on the stakeholders is shown in Table 12.1-1.

     As the project is still in the preparatory phase, the stakeholders in the implementation and

closed.

12.2      Stakeholder Engagement and Information Disclosure during the
Preparation Period
12.2.1 Stakeholder engagement activities undertaken
     Stakeholder engagement and consultation activities for this project started at the project
identification stage and will continue until project closure. To date, the PMO has organized a

                                                     125
series of stakeholder engagement and consultation activities. The highlights of the engagement
and consultation activities during the project preparation phase are as follows.

     (1) Collect opinions and suggestions from relevant departments on the project and
optimize the project design.

        The project preparation stage has repeatedly organized talks and consultations between
relevant authorities and consultants for feasibility studies, environmental assessment and social
assessment, etc., to identify project construction needs, policy requirements, procedure
requirements, etc., and to listen to the opinions of relevant departments to optimize the project
design, such as (1) the forestry department suggests that the project avoids the forest land on
the northwest side, to reduce the impact of the project on the important habitats and forest land,
and optimize the project design and siting in this regard, and the main route of the greenway
was adjusted accordingly. (2) The ecology and environmental protection department mentioned
the ecological buffer zone control requirements of the project's regional management strategy
and the wetland into the lake, which were considered in the project. The statistics of
stakeholder engagement activities are shown in the following table.

                                                       130
(2) Consultation on environmental issues and identification of environmental issues of
public concern

     The project conducted a public consultation on November 29-30, 2024, to understand the
attitudes and concerns of the residents in the project area about the project, to optimize the
project management and environmental protection measures during the subsequent project
implementation, and the content of the public consultant is shown in Table 11.2-1. The
questionnaire contains the basic information of the respondents, such as gender, age,
educational background, occupation, etc., and the statistical information is shown in Table
11.2-2. The results of the questionnaire survey are shown in Table 11.2-3, and the results of the
survey show that: (1) most people said that they did not know about the project before the
public consultation; (2) most people said that they were concerned about how to develop Lake
Aha after it was withdrawn from the protected area for drinking water sources; (3) during the
construction stage of the project, people are mainly concerned about surface water, ecology,
and solid waste, and one respondent expressed concern about traffic safety during the
construction period; during the operation period, they are mainly concerned about atmospheric
pollution such as automobile exhaust, traffic noise, and solid waste pollution, etc.; (4) The vast
majority of the people agree with the siting and routing of the project; (5) All of the
respondents have a supportive attitude towards the project, and they believe that the
construction of the project will have a positive local economic impact.

I. Introduction to the project
       (i) Project name: Guiyang Green Urban Development Project
       (ii) Project authority: Guiyang City Urban Construction Investment Group Co.
       (iii) Location of project construction: Lake Aha region
       (iv) Duration of project construction: expected to be 2026-2030, with an estimated duration of five
years.
       (v) Overall project development objectives: The project's objectives are to reduce greenhouse gas
emissions through the implementation of green measures in urban areas, to increase carbon sequestration
through the restoration of ecosystem productivity, and to enhance the protection and sustainable
management of land areas and inland water areas for nature-positive urban development.
       Given that a single project cannot achieve all of Guiyang's nature-positive goals and address all
climate-related issues, this project uses Guiyang City's Lake Aha as a target area to demonstrate an
integrated approach to achieving these goals, complemented by low-carbon platforms, systems, policies,
research, and fundamental monitoring and evaluation activities that encompass the entire city of Guiyang.
       (vi) Main construction elements of the project:
       1, low-carbon urban transportation projects: Lake Aha Lake Greenway, upgrading of Jinzhu Road


                                                       131
(North), Jinzhu Road (South), Jingshan Road, Shangba Access Road, and C416, Zhulin Village Bus
Terminal, parking lot construction project, Jinzhu North Interchange and the Access Road, Jinzhu North
Interchange with the West Second Ring Access Road construction project.
      2. Biodiversity protection projects: (1) Lake Aha Wetland Park biodiversity monitoring and protection,
bird habitat restoration, Lake Aha Basin Ecological Buffer Zone Restoration, and the Lanni Gully River
Channel Management Project. (2) Lake Aha Interceptor Ditch and Lifting Pumping Station Construction
Project, Xiaoche River Basin Interceptor Upgrading and Improvement, Lanni Gully Diversion, Baiyan River
and Youyu River Basin Rural Water Pollution Prevention and Control Project. (3) Lake Aha Public Facilities
River Infrastructure: including the construction of stations around the lake, landscape greening, wetland
nature education and supporting service facilities.
       3. Innovative methods, systems and capacity strengthening.
      (vii) Investment Estimation: The total investment of the project is about RMB 2.44559 billion, of which
RMB 1.8 billion is loaned by the World Bank (equivalent to about US$250 million according to the
exchange rate of US$ to RMB 1:7.2), and RMB 645.59 million is domestic counterpart funds.

12.3     Stakeholder Engagement and Consultation Program
12.3.1 Public Consultation
    According to the requirements of the WB and drawing on the experience of similar


                                            135
projects in China, the distribution of questionnaires, symposiums, visits to relevant departments
and other ways were conducted for public participation to solve difficult problems for the
public and answer questions to solve environmental protection and mitigation measures. The
appraisal phase, construction period and operation period of this project fully understand the
public's opinion on the impact of the project and the degree of satisfaction with the
environmental impact mitigation measures. In addition, the stakeholder coordination activities
planned for the project should also include the following elements: (1) Consultation on
environmental protection of Lake Aha Wetland Park. The PMO organizes the contractors and
the management office of Lake Aha Wetland Park to understand the environmental protection
requirements of the wetland park, zoning control requirements and other notable issues for
construction within the wetland park. The environmental protection supervision department
should be invited to understand the implementation of environmental protection personnel,
institutions and measures, the discharge of pollutants up to standards, and whether
environmental protection measures need to be optimized and adjusted. (2) Coordination of
construction with reservoir dam safety and reservoir water level scheduling. The PMO
organizes contractors and Lake Aha Wetland Park Management Office, Dam Management
Office, wetland experts, ecological protection experts, etc., to discuss how to coordinate the
scheduling of the reservoir water level with the construction, the relationship between the
reservoir scheduling and the wetland park's biodiversity protection, and how to dispatch and
regulate the water level to be more conducive to the project area's ecological environmental
protection and restoration. (3) Traffic organization plan and road safety management measures
during the construction period of the road project. The PMO organizes the contractors, traffic
control department, listens to the opinions and suggestions of the surrounding residents, etc., to
formulate and implement the traffic organization plan and road safety management measures
during the construction period. Detailed plan is shown in Table 11.3-1.

12.3.1 Information Disclosure Schedule
     The proposed information disclosure is shown in Table 11.3-2. The disclosure program is
dynamic. During the course of the project, the PMO updates the implementation of this plan
and maintains a complete record of all disclosures to facilitate access to project information by
other stakeholders during project implementation or after project completion.

13. Conclusions

13.1     Project Overview
     This project is Guiyang Green Urban Development Project funded by the World Bank
loans, covering the physical investments of greenway, cycling stations and bus transportation
facilities around the lake, urban road improvement, wetland and landscape restoration, as well
as the technical assistance activities for the development of Guiyang low carbon smart platform
and green account, low-carbon and nature-positive spatial planning, related research and other
capacity strengthening activities. The project’s total investment is estimated as 2.64168 billion
yuan, with the construction period of 5 years (2026-2030).

13.2      Environment baseline
     Air quality: According to the "2023 Guiyang City Ecological and Environmental
Conditions Bulletin", the ambient air quality in Guiyang City reaches the Class II standard of
"Ambient Air Quality Standard" (GB3095-2012), and the ambient air quality of the project
area meets the standard requirements.

     Surface water: except for the TN and TN exceeding the standard in the project area of
Lanni Gully and the big lake, all other water bodies meet the standard limit of Category III of
the Environmental Quality Standard for Surface Water (GB3838-2002).

     Acoustic environment: According to the status quo monitoring, the acoustic environment
quality of each monitoring point of the project can reach the limit value of Category 2 standard
of Acoustic Environment Quality Standard (GB3096-2008), and the regional acoustic
environment quality is good.

13.3      Environmental Benefits
     The project implementation will promote the environmental improvements and ecological
protection in the Lake Aha Basin, facilitate Guiyang's green and low-carbon development, and
enhance the city's climate resilience and adaptation capacity.

       13.3.1 Reduction of carbon emissions and increase of carbon sinks
     The construction of the project's transportation facilities will improve transportation
efficiency and increase the proportion of public transportation, thus reducing carbon emissions.
In addition, planning and control, restoration of forest and wetland ecosystems, and upgrading
the quality of the water environment will continue to improve the ecosystem's ability to
sequester carbon.


                                                 141
       13.3.2 Improvement of water environment quality in the lake basin
     The project will construct 22.2km kilometers of interception pipeline and 7 lifting pump
stations to transport wastewater to the wastewater treatment plant for unified treatment. At the
same time, the project will carry out the rural water pollution control of Baiyan River and
Youyu River basin, constructing 27.6km of wastewater pipe network and 8 wastewater
treatment stations and other water treatment and pollution control facilities to improve the
water quality of Lake Aha. After the completion of the project, the regional wastewater
collection rate can be increased from the current 50% to 100%, and the centralized treatment
rate can be increased from the current 30% to 70%; in the near future, the annual reduction of
BOD will be 1,873 tons, and the reduction of COD will be 2,535 tons, which will effectively
improve the water quality of the Lake Aha region.

       13.3.3 Restoration of bird habitats
     The bird habitat restoration works of Lake Aha National Wetland Park covers an area of
53.29 hectares in Kailong Village in the northwestern part of the park facing the mountain and
the lake branch of the reservoir in the southern part of the park, and restores the structure and
quantity of plant and animal communities, improves the heterogeneity and suitability of the
bird habitat, further enriches the diversity of birds, and improves the wetland ecosystem's
self-sustaining ability through the prevention, control and management of pollutants, ecological
restoration works, and the creation of a micro-habitat. In addition, the project also establishes a
biomonitoring system to monitor bird habitats, to grasp the dynamics of bird populations and
habitat changes in real time, and to better carry out conservation work.

       13.3.4 Enhancement of ecosystem functions
     The implementation of the project will increase the forest area through forest vegetation
restoration and enhance the quality of wetland ecosystems through ecological restoration,
which can improve the carbon sequestration capacity of forest and wetland ecosystems and
significantly increase carbon sinks. In addition, the project will have the following positive
effects on ecosystem service functions:

     （1） Enhancement of regulating service functions

     Forests and wetland vegetation play a role in intercepting rainwater through the forest
canopy, the shrub and grass layer, the withered leaf layer and the soil layer, reducing surface
runoff and runoff velocity and weakening the erosive force of rainfall on the surface, thus
preventing soil erosion and soil loss. Enriching vegetation communities can also further



                                                 142
improve soil structure and play a role in water conservation and water purification. New and
improved forest and wetland vegetation can also purify the air, improve regional air quality,
increase carbon sinks and regulate temperature and climate.

     （2） Enhancement of cultural services

     The project carries out activities such as forest vegetation restoration, interception of
pollution to improve water quality, and shoreline restoration, and create natural cultural
landscape nodes, science education nodes, nodes with local characteristics, etc. The overall
landscape of the project area will be improved and take on the functions of science
popularization and education, tourism and sightseeing.

     （3） Enhancement of support service functions:

     By increasing the area of forests and upgrading the quality of forests and wetlands, the
soil structure can be improved, the improvement and cycling of soil nutrient can be promoted,
and the level of primary productivity of ecosystems can be increased, which creates conditions
for the maintenance and enhancement of biodiversity. At the same time, the increase in biomass,
such as vegetation, will also improve the level of oxygen supply.

13.4      General conclusions on environmental impact analysis
     The environmental and social risk of this project is deemed Substantial considering some
of the project activities designed and to be implemented within the scope of Aha Lake National
Wetland Park and Guiyang’s delineated ecological red line. However, these activities are
designed in alignment with the local ecological conservation plan and national regulations on
ecological red line management and biodiversity protection. During construction and operation,
the project is anticipated to bring temporary and site-specific negative environmental impacts,
for example, construction nuisance, risks associated with pesticide use and increased traffic and
so on. An EMP has been prepared as part of current EIA to outline the mitigation measures
which are deemed adequate to address these negative environmental impacts. With the
proposed mitigation measures taken, no significant residual impacts are anticipated resulting
from the project implementation. The draft EIA and EMP have been consulted and disclosed
locally during preparation. The feedback shows that the project is generally supported by the
public.

     At the same time, the PMO has engaged Guiyang City Transportation Planning Survey
Design Institute Co., Ltd to conduct a more detailed Domestic Environmental Impact



                                                143
Assessment (DEIA) for the project, along with the studies to justify the adjustments of forest
land categorization, the impact assessment for Aha Wetland Park, and the permission for
limited human activities within the ecological protection red line, as well as the site-specific
biodiversity impact assessment, etc. Now these assessments and studies have already gained
the approval and consent from the various competent authorities (see Section 3.3.1 of this
report for details).
